Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
Definition and Ruling of Divorce
Definition and ruling of divorce with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of divorce, identify its ruling (hukm) with proofs, and distinguish its conditions and pillars.

Core Idea
Divorce is the removal of the marriage bond; it is permissible but the most detestable of permissible things.

The Book of Divorce begins with a precise legal definition: divorce (talaq) is the removal of the marriage bond established by shari‘ah. This lesson unpacks that definition, the default ruling of permissibility (ibahah), and the essential conditions and pillars. You will also learn the Quranic proofs that establish divorce as a legislated institution, contrary to a minority view that restricts it to necessity.

Guided Path
1
1. Understand the definition
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions. Note that legally it is 'removing the bond established by marriage', distinguishing it from physical release (untying a rope) and from emancipation (which removes a bond not through marriage).
The linguistic origin is 'releasing a camel from its hobble'.
2
2. Identify the ruling (hukm)
The default ruling is ibahah (permissibility). However, divorce is described as abghadh al-mubahat (the most detestable of permissible things). Its hukm can change: recommended (mustahabb) if the wife is harmful or neglects prayer, obligatory (wajib) if retention with kindness is impossible, and prohibited (haram) if it is bid‘i (innovative).
The permissibility is established by Quranic verses (65:1, 2:236) and the practice of the Prophet and Companions.
3
3. List the conditions (shurut) and pillar (rukn)
Conditions for validity: the husband must be legally responsible (mukallaf) even constructively (e.g., drunkard); the wife must be married or in a revocable waiting period. The pillar (rukn) is the utterance itself (sighah).
The cause (sabab) is the need for relief when spouses are incompatible.
4
4. Address the contrary view
Some argue divorce is only allowed for necessity, citing hadiths that condemn frequent divorce. The Hanafi response: the Quran explicitly permits divorce (2:236 uses 'la junaha' = no sin), and the Prophet and Companions divorced without censure.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

(ع ، مس] المناسبة بين كتاب الطلاق وكتاب الرضاع: أن الطلاق محرم كالرضاع، والمناسبة بين الطلاق والنكاح التقابل والتضاد، وقدم الرضاع؛ لأن حرمته مؤبدة، والطلاق مغيا بغاية، وتقديم الأشد أسد، وإيقاع الطلاق مباح، ومن الناس من يقول: لا يباح إلا للضرورة؛ لقوله عليه: "لعن الله كل ذواق مطلاق"، وقال له: "أبغض الحلال إلى الله تعالى الطلاق، وقال: لا تطلقوا النساء إلا من ربيبة إن الله لا يحب الذواقين ولا الذواقات، وقال: زوجوا ولا تطلقوا، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِّقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ (الطلاق: 1) وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ ﴾ (البقرة : ٢٣٦) هذا يقتضي الإباحة، وطلق رسول الله الله ، حفصة، والصحابة كانوا يطلقون من غير نكير. ( عيني، فتح، زيلعي) رفع القيد: وسببه الحاجة إلى الخلاص عند تباين الأخلاق وشرطه كون الزوج مكلفاً ولو تقديراً كسكران، وكون المرأة منكوحة أو في عدة تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق، وحكمه وقوع الفرقة مؤجلاً بانقضاء العدة في الرجعي، وبدونه في البائن، وركنه نفس اللفظ، ووصفه الإباحة للتخلص به من المكاره الدينية والدنيوية، وهو أبغض المباحات وجعلت ولايته إلى الرجل؛ لأنه المالك كالمسترق لها بالمهر؛ ولأنها لا روية لها في أمورها، و شرع ا العدد فيه للتمكن من التدارك عند الندم وانحصر في الثلاث؛ لأنه عدد متعين في الشرع، وهو أقل الجمع؛ ولا نهاية لأكثره، ويستحب الطلاق لو مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة، ويجب لو فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في المحبوب والعنين، ويحرم لو كان الطلاق بدعياً. (عيني، فتح)
شرعاً: احترز به عن رفع القيد الثابت حساً وهو حل الوثاق. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣١/١] بالنكاح احترز به عن العتق؛ لأنه رفع قيد ثابت شرعا لكنه لا بالنكاح (ع) تطليقها إلخ: [مرفوع بالابتداء، مصدر مضاف إلى المفعول تقديره تطليق الرجل امرأته مبتدأ، وأحسن خبره أي أحسن الطلاق يطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه ولا في الحيض الذي قبله ويتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها، وإنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الحسن؛ لأنه لا خلاف لأحد في عدم الكراهة فيه بخلاف الحسن، فإن مالكاً يقول فيه بالكراهة، ومعنى كونه أحسن أي بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن، وكيف يكون حسناً في نفسه مع أنه أبغض المباح، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون؛ فإن الطلاق المسنون حسن وأحسن، ومعنى المسنون والسني هنا أنه ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المتعقب للثواب؛ لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه. (مص، فتح) وتركها بالرفع عطف على المبتدأ مضاف إلى المفعول والفاعل متروك أي وترك هذا المطلق امرأته. (ع)

حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن، وثلاثاً في أطهار حسن وسنّي، وثلاثاً في طهر أو بكلمةٍ بدعي
أي إلى أن تنقضي أحسن: خبر المبتدأ؛ لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أن الصحابة كانوا يستحبون أن لا يزيدوا في الطلاق على واحدة حتى تمضي عدتها؛ ولأنه أبعد من الندم لتمكنه من التدارك. (ع)
:
أطهار أي تطليقها ثلاث طلقات متفرقة في ثلاثة أطهار لا وطء فيها في كل طهر واحد للمدخول بها. (ط، ع) حسن وسني: [من حيث الوقت والعدد ثم قيل: الأولى أن يؤخر الإيقاع إلى آخر وقت الطهر احترازا عن تطويل العدة، والأظهر أن يطلقها كما طهرت (ط)] يعني الطلاق الحسن والسني أن يطلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار، وإذا كان الحسن سنياً فلأن يكون الأحسن سنياً بالأولى. واعلم أن السنة في الطلاق على نوعين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد. فالسنة في الوقت لا يثبت إلا بالمدخول بها خاصة وهو أن يطلقها واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه كما مر والسنة في العدد يستوي فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها؛ لأن السنة في العدد هو أن يطلقها واحدة فإن كانت في الموطوءة في طهر خال عن الجماع يكون سنياً في العدد والوقت.
وإن لم يكن في طهر خال عن الجماع وهو سني في العدد وبدعي في الوقت، وإذا طلق غير المدخول بها واحدة يقع سنيا سواء كان في الحيض أو الطهر؛ لأن الرغبة متجددة فيها على كل حال، بخلاف الموطوءة؛ لأن زمان الحيض زمان النفرة عنها، وأيضاً بالجماع مرة في طهر تقل الرغبة إليها، وقال مالك: التطليق ثلاثاً في أطهار بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق محظور فلا يباح الإقدام عليه إلا لدفع الحاجة وهو يحصل بالواحدة ولنا: قوله عليه لعمر ه: مر ابنك فليراجعها، ثم يدعها حتى تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها ثم تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها إن أحب"، وقال عليها: "إن من السنة أن يستقبل الطهر استقبالاً فيطلقها بكل قرء تطليقة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وثلاثاً : أي تطليقها ثلاثاً متفرقة في طهر واحد (ط) أو بكلمة واحدة بأن قال: أنت طالق ثلاثاً في طهر، أو جمع بين التطليقتين في طهر بكلمة أو بكلمتين لم يتخلل بينهما رجعة. (ط،ع) بدعي: [من . حيث العدد سني من حيث الوقت إن خلا الطهر عن الجماع. (ط، ع)] أي منسوب إلى البدعة من حيث العدد؛ لما روي في حديث ابن عمر له قال : قلت: يا رسول الله ! أرأيت لو طلقتها ثلاثاً؟" قال: "إذا قد عصيت ربك وبانت منك امرأتك"، رواه ابن أبي شيبة والدار قطني، والمراد بقوله: "ثلاثاً في طهر" أنه لم يتخلل بين التطليقتين رجعة وإن تخلل فلا يكره عند أبي حنيفة رحاله ، وإن تخلل التزوج بينهما فلا يكره بالإجماع، وقال الشافعي: لا تكون الثلاث في طهر واحد أو في كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق مشروع، والمشروعية لا يجامع الحظر بخلاف الطلاق في حالة الحيض؛ لأن الحرام تطويل العدة لا الطلاق والحجة عليه ما روينا، فإذا طلق ثلاثا في طهر أو بكلمة وقع الطلاق وصار عاصياً، وذهب جماعة منهم الظاهرية والشيعة إلى أن الطلاق الثلاث جملة لا تقع إلا واحدة؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه قال: كان الطلاق على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر، وسنتين ما واحدة فأمضاه عليهم عمر ه ، رواه مسلم والبخاري ولنا ما روي من حديث العجلاني، = من خلافة عمر
The Book of Divorce. That is, in explanation of its rulings. It is the removal of the bond established legally through marriage. Divorcing her once in a pure state (tuhr) in which there was no intercourse, and leaving her. That is, divorce. That is, one divorce, attached to the subject. The Book of Divorce: [Linguistically, it is the removal of a bond absolutely, derived from releasing a camel, i.e., sending it from its hobble. It is a verbal noun meaning 'divorcing', like 'salam' meaning 'surrendering'. Legally, it is what the author mentioned. (Ayni, Musannaf)] The connection between the Book of Divorce and the Book of Breastfeeding: divorce is prohibited like breastfeeding. The connection between divorce and marriage is opposition and contrast. He prioritized breastfeeding because its prohibition is permanent, while divorce has a fixed term, and prioritizing the stronger is more sound. Performing divorce is permissible. Some people say: it is not permissible except for necessity, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Allah curses every frequent divorcer and frequent wife-taker', and he said: 'The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce', and he said: 'Do not divorce women except for open lewdness; Allah does not love those who often divorce and often take wives', and he said: 'Marry and do not divorce.' Our proof is Allah's statement: {And when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period} (65:1) and {There is no blame upon you if you divorce women} (2:236). This implies permissibility. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, divorced Hafsah, and the Companions used to divorce without any objection. (Ayni, Fath, Zaylai). Removal of the bond: its cause is the need for release when dispositions differ. Its condition is that the husband be legally responsible, even constructively like a drunkard, and that the woman be married or in a waiting period in which she is fit to be a place for divorce. Its ruling is the occurrence of separation, deferred by the expiry of the waiting period in a revocable divorce, and immediate in an irrevocable divorce. Its pillar is the utterance itself. Its description is permissibility to rid oneself of religious and worldly dislikes, and it is the most detestable of permissible things. Its authority is given to the man because he is the owner, like one who acquires her through the mahr, and because she has no deliberation in her affairs. The number of it is legislated to enable reconsideration upon regret, and it is limited to three because it is a number fixed in law, and it is the smallest plural; there is no maximum to its greater number. Divorce is recommended if she is harmful or abandons prayer, and obligatory if retaining her with kindness is not possible, as in the case of one who hates her and the impotent man. It is prohibited if the divorce is bid'i (innovative). (Ayni, Fath). Legally: excludes the removal of a bond established physically, i.e., untying a rope. By marriage: excludes emancipation, because it is the removal of a bond legally established but not through marriage. (Ayni). Divorcing her etc.: [Raised as the subject, a verbal noun attached to the object, its implied construction: the man divorcing his wife is the subject, and 'ahsan' (best) is its predicate, meaning the best form of divorce is that the man divorces his wife with one divorce in a pure state (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her nor in the preceding menstruation, and leaves her until her waiting period expires. This category is better than 'hasan' (good) because there is no disagreement about the absence of dislike (karaha) in it, unlike 'hasan', for which Malik says there is dislike. The meaning of it being better is relative to the other part, not that it is good in itself; how can it be good in itself when it is the most detestable of permissible things? This is one of the two types of sunnah divorce: the sunnah divorce is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of 'sunnah' and 'sunni' here is that it is established in a manner that does not incur blame, not that it is followed by reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself. (Musaffa, Fath). And 'leaving her' in the nominative is a conjunction to the subject attached to the object, the agent is omitted, i.e., this divorcer leaves his wife. (Ayni). Sections of Divorce and Their Rulings. ...until her waiting period expires is 'ahsan' (best). And three in pure states is 'hasan' (good) and 'sunni' (according to Sunnah). And three in one pure state or by one word is 'bid'i' (innovative). That is, until she completes it: 'ahsan' is the predicate of the subject; because it was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions used to prefer not to increase divorce beyond one until her waiting period expires, and because it is farthest from regret due to enabling reconsideration. (Ayni). Pure states: i.e., divorcing her with three separate divorces in three pure states without intercourse, one in each tuhr for the one who has been entered. (Talwi, Ayni). 'Hasan' and 'sunni': [regarding time and number. Then it was said: the first is to delay the pronouncement to the end of the tuhr to avoid prolonging the waiting period. The more apparent is to divorce her as soon as she becomes pure. (Talwi)] Meaning, the 'hasan' and 'sunni' divorce is to divorce her three times in three pure states. And if 'hasan' is sunni, then it follows that 'ahsan' is sunni. Know that Sunnah in divorce is of two types: Sunnah in time, and Sunnah in number. The Sunnah in time is only established for the one who has been entered, and it is to divorce her once in a pure state in which he has not had intercourse with her, as passed. The Sunnah in number applies equally to the one who has been entered and the one who has not, because the Sunnah in number is to divorce her once. If it is in the one who has been entered in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in both number and time. If it is not in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in number and bid'i in time. If one divorces the one not entered once, it occurs as sunni whether in menstruation or purity, because desire for her is renewed in every state, unlike the one entered, because the time of menstruation is a time of aversion from her, and also because once intercourse in a tuhr reduces desire for her. Malik said: divorcing three times in pure states is bid'a because divorce is prohibited, so one should not proceed except to fulfill a need, which is achieved with one. Our proof: his statement, peace be upon him, to Umar: 'Order your son to take her back, then leave her until she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her, then she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her if he wishes.' And he said, peace be upon him: 'It is from the Sunnah to approach the pure state directly, and divorce her with each period a divorce.' (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni). And three: i.e., divorcing her three separate times in one pure state (Talwi) or by one word, by saying: 'You are divorced thrice' in a tuhr, or combining two divorces in a tuhr by one word or two words without a revocation in between. (Talwi, Ayni). Bid'i: [regarding number, sunni regarding time if the tuhr is free from intercourse. (Talwi, Ayni)] i.e., attributed to innovation regarding number; due to the narration of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, what if I divorced her three times? He said: 'Then you would have disobeyed your Lord, and she would be irrevocably separated from you.' Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah and al-Daraqutni. The meaning of his statement 'three in a tuhr' is that no revocation occurs between the two divorces; if revocation occurs, it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. If remarriage occurs between them, it is not disliked by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: Three divorces in one tuhr or by one word are not bid'a because divorce is legislated, and legislation is not compatible with prohibition, unlike divorce during menstruation, because the prohibited thing is prolonging the waiting period, not divorce. The proof against him is what we have narrated. So if he divorces three times in a tuhr or by one word, the divorce occurs and he becomes sinful. A group, including the Zahiris and Shi'ah, hold that three divorces together only count as one, due to the narration from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: Divorce was one at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and Abu Bakr, and two years of Umar's caliphate, then Umar enforced it as three. Reported by Muslim and al-Bukhari. Our proof is the narration from the 'Ujlayni hadith, = from the caliphate of Umar.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Talaq with a comprehensive definition and classification. The author defines divorce (talaq) as the removal of the marriage bond established by shari'ah. Linguistically, it is derived from releasing a camel from its hobble; legally, it is as the author states. The placement of Talaq after the book of Radha' (breastfeeding) is justified: both involve prohibition, but divorce is temporary while radha' is permanent, so the stronger is placed first. The ruling on divorce is ibahah (permissibility), though there is a minority view that it is only for necessity, citing hadiths that condemn divorce. The Hanafi position relies on clear Quranic verses (65:1 and 2:236) that imply permission, the Prophet's own divorce of Hafsah, and the general practice of the Companions without censure. Divorce is the most detestable of permissible things (abghadh al-mubahat). Its cause is the need for relief when spouses are incompatible; its condition for the husband is legal responsibility (taklif) even constructively for a drunkard; for the wife, she must be married or in a revocable waiting period; its ruling is the occurrence of separation (firqah), deferred in revocable divorce (raj'i) until iddah ends, immediate in irrevocable (ba'in); its pillar (rukn) is the utterance itself. The number of pronouncements is limited to three because it is a legally fixed number and the smallest plural; there is no maximum number of three. Divorce is recommended (mustahabb) if the wife is harmful or neglects prayer; obligatory (wajib) if retaining her with kindness is impossible, as in cases of extreme aversion or impotence; and prohibited (haram) if it is bid'i (innovative). The passage then details the three categories of divorce based on time and number: Ahsan (best): one pronouncement in a tuhr (pure period) with no intercourse, followed by leaving her to complete her iddah. This is agreed upon without dislike. Hasan (good): three pronouncements in three separate tuhrs. This is sunnah in time and number, though Imam Malik considers it disliked. Bid'i (innovative): three pronouncements in one tuhr (either separately without revocation in between) or by a single phrase. This is sinful (ma'siyah) but the divorce takes effect. Al-Shafi'i argues this is not bid'i because divorce is legislated and legislation cannot combine with prohibition; the Hanafi response cites the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet said three divorces in one tuhr make her irrevocable and constitute disobedience. The passage also notes that some (Zahiris, Shi'ah) hold that triple divorce counts as one, relying on the practice of the early caliphate, but the Hanafis reject this with other narrations. The teacher should emphasize that while divorce is permitted, it is most disliked, and the sunnah methods (ahsan and hasan) are prescribed to allow opportunity for reconciliation. The bid'i method is sinful yet effective—a critical distinction in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Legally, the removal of the marriage bond established by shari'ah; linguistically, releasing an animal from its hobble.
مُكَلَّف (mukallaf): Legally responsible; one who is adult and sane, capable of bearing religious obligations.
أبغض المباحات (abghadh al-mubahat): The most detestable of permissible things; a description of divorce emphasizing its strong dislike despite being lawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default ruling (hukm asli) of divorce in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Haram (prohibited)
B) Makruh tahrimi (reprehensible bordering on prohibited)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Sunnah (recommended)

Key Takeaway
Divorce is legally defined as the removal of the marriage bond; it is permissible but most disliked, and its validity depends on the husband's legal capacity and clear utterance.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The Three Categories of Divorce: Ahsan, Hasan, and Bid‘i
Classification of divorce into three types based on time and number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of divorce in Hanafi fiqh (ahsan, hasan, bid‘i) based on time and number, and explain which are sunnah and which are bid‘a.

Core Idea
The best divorce is one pronouncement in a pure state; three in separate pure states is good; three at once is sinful but effective.

Divorce is not a single act; the Hanafi school classifies it into three categories based on how many pronouncements are made and in what time frame. The best (ahsan) leaves the door open for reconciliation, the good (hasan) follows a slower process, and the innovative (bid‘i) is sinful though legally binding. This lesson unpacks each category, explaining the sunnah in time and number, and the points of disagreement with other schools.

Guided Path
1
1. Understand the sunnah divorce types
Sunnah divorce is of two types: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. The best (ahsan) fulfills both: one pronouncement in a tuhr free from intercourse. The good (hasan) is sunnah in number but the three pronouncements occur in three separate tuhrs, making it also sunnah in time (though some differences exist about the exact timing).
The passage explains that for the non-consummated wife, even divorce during menstruation is sunni in number.
2
2. Distinguish ahsan from hasan
Ahsan is one pronouncement followed by leaving her until iddah ends; there is no dislike (karahah) in it from any school. Hasan is three pronouncements in three separate tuhrs; Imam Malik holds it is disliked (bid‘a), but Hanafis consider it sunnah.
The passage mentions the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet instructed Umar to order his son to take his wife back and then divorce her after each tuhr.
3
3. Identify bid‘i divorce
Bid‘i divorce is three pronouncements in one tuhr (either by separate statements without revocation in between, or by a single phrase). It is sinful (the husband disobeys Allah) but the divorce takes effect as three irrevocable divorces.
The hadith of Ibn Umar: 'If you do that, you have disobeyed your Lord and she becomes irrevocably separated.'
4
4. Note the cross-madhhab differences
Al-Shafi‘i does not consider triple divorce in one tuhr as bid‘i; he argues that legislation cannot combine with prohibition. The Hanafi response is the explicit hadith. Also, Zahiris and Shi‘ah hold that triple divorce counts as one, but Hanafis reject this.
This will be covered in more detail in the next lesson.

كتاب الطلاق: [هو لغة رفع القيد مطلقاً مأخوذ من إطلاق البعير وهو إرساله . من عقاله، ومصدر بمعنى التطليق كالسلام بمعنى التسليم وشرعا ما ذكره المصنف. (ع ، مس] المناسبة بين كتاب الطلاق وكتاب الرضاع: أن الطلاق محرم كالرضاع، والمناسبة بين الطلاق والنكاح التقابل والتضاد، وقدم الرضاع؛ لأن حرمته مؤبدة، والطلاق مغيا بغاية، وتقديم الأشد أسد، وإيقاع الطلاق مباح، ومن الناس من يقول: لا يباح إلا للضرورة؛ لقوله عليه: "لعن الله كل ذواق مطلاق"، وقال له: "أبغض الحلال إلى الله تعالى الطلاق، وقال: لا تطلقوا النساء إلا من ربيبة إن الله لا يحب الذواقين ولا الذواقات، وقال: زوجوا ولا تطلقوا، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِّقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ (الطلاق: 1) وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ ﴾ (البقرة : ٢٣٦) هذا يقتضي الإباحة، وطلق رسول الله الله ، حفصة، والصحابة كانوا يطلقون من غير نكير. ( عيني، فتح، زيلعي) رفع القيد: وسببه الحاجة إلى الخلاص عند تباين الأخلاق وشرطه كون الزوج مكلفاً ولو تقديراً كسكران، وكون المرأة منكوحة أو في عدة تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق، وحكمه وقوع الفرقة مؤجلاً بانقضاء العدة في الرجعي، وبدونه في البائن، وركنه نفس اللفظ، ووصفه الإباحة للتخلص به من المكاره الدينية والدنيوية، وهو أبغض المباحات وجعلت ولايته إلى الرجل؛ لأنه المالك كالمسترق لها بالمهر؛ ولأنها لا روية لها في أمورها، و شرع ا العدد فيه للتمكن من التدارك عند الندم وانحصر في الثلاث؛ لأنه عدد متعين في الشرع، وهو أقل الجمع؛ ولا نهاية لأكثره، ويستحب الطلاق لو مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة، ويجب لو فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في المحبوب والعنين، ويحرم لو كان الطلاق بدعياً. (عيني، فتح)
شرعاً: احترز به عن رفع القيد الثابت حساً وهو حل الوثاق. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣١/١] بالنكاح احترز به عن العتق؛ لأنه رفع قيد ثابت شرعا لكنه لا بالنكاح (ع) تطليقها إلخ: [مرفوع بالابتداء، مصدر مضاف إلى المفعول تقديره تطليق الرجل امرأته مبتدأ، وأحسن خبره أي أحسن الطلاق يطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه ولا في الحيض الذي قبله ويتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها، وإنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الحسن؛ لأنه لا خلاف لأحد في عدم الكراهة فيه بخلاف الحسن، فإن مالكاً يقول فيه بالكراهة، ومعنى كونه أحسن أي بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن، وكيف يكون حسناً في نفسه مع أنه أبغض المباح، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون؛ فإن الطلاق المسنون حسن وأحسن، ومعنى المسنون والسني هنا أنه ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المتعقب للثواب؛ لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه. (مص، فتح) وتركها بالرفع عطف على المبتدأ مضاف إلى المفعول والفاعل متروك أي وترك هذا المطلق امرأته. (ع)

:
أطهار أي تطليقها ثلاث طلقات متفرقة في ثلاثة أطهار لا وطء فيها في كل طهر واحد للمدخول بها. (ط، ع) حسن وسني: [من حيث الوقت والعدد ثم قيل: الأولى أن يؤخر الإيقاع إلى آخر وقت الطهر احترازا عن تطويل العدة، والأظهر أن يطلقها كما طهرت (ط)] يعني الطلاق الحسن والسني أن يطلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار، وإذا كان الحسن سنياً فلأن يكون الأحسن سنياً بالأولى. واعلم أن السنة في الطلاق على نوعين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد. فالسنة في الوقت لا يثبت إلا بالمدخول بها خاصة وهو أن يطلقها واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه كما مر والسنة في العدد يستوي فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها؛ لأن السنة في العدد هو أن يطلقها واحدة فإن كانت في الموطوءة في طهر خال عن الجماع يكون سنياً في العدد والوقت.
وإن لم يكن في طهر خال عن الجماع وهو سني في العدد وبدعي في الوقت، وإذا طلق غير المدخول بها واحدة يقع سنيا سواء كان في الحيض أو الطهر؛ لأن الرغبة متجددة فيها على كل حال، بخلاف الموطوءة؛ لأن زمان الحيض زمان النفرة عنها، وأيضاً بالجماع مرة في طهر تقل الرغبة إليها، وقال مالك: التطليق ثلاثاً في أطهار بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق محظور فلا يباح الإقدام عليه إلا لدفع الحاجة وهو يحصل بالواحدة ولنا: قوله عليه لعمر ه: مر ابنك فليراجعها، ثم يدعها حتى تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها ثم تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها إن أحب"، وقال عليها: "إن من السنة أن يستقبل الطهر استقبالاً فيطلقها بكل قرء تطليقة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وثلاثاً : أي تطليقها ثلاثاً متفرقة في طهر واحد (ط) أو بكلمة واحدة بأن قال: أنت طالق ثلاثاً في طهر، أو جمع بين التطليقتين في طهر بكلمة أو بكلمتين لم يتخلل بينهما رجعة. (ط،ع) بدعي: [من . حيث العدد سني من حيث الوقت إن خلا الطهر عن الجماع. (ط، ع)] أي منسوب إلى البدعة من حيث العدد؛ لما روي في حديث ابن عمر له قال : قلت: يا رسول الله ! أرأيت لو طلقتها ثلاثاً؟" قال: "إذا قد عصيت ربك وبانت منك امرأتك"، رواه ابن أبي شيبة والدار قطني، والمراد بقوله: "ثلاثاً في طهر" أنه لم يتخلل بين التطليقتين رجعة وإن تخلل فلا يكره عند أبي حنيفة رحاله ، وإن تخلل التزوج بينهما فلا يكره بالإجماع، وقال الشافعي: لا تكون الثلاث في طهر واحد أو في كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق مشروع، والمشروعية لا يجامع الحظر بخلاف الطلاق في حالة الحيض؛ لأن الحرام تطويل العدة لا الطلاق والحجة عليه ما روينا، فإذا طلق ثلاثا في طهر أو بكلمة وقع الطلاق وصار عاصياً، وذهب جماعة منهم الظاهرية والشيعة إلى أن الطلاق الثلاث جملة لا تقع إلا واحدة؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه قال: كان الطلاق على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر، وسنتين ما واحدة فأمضاه عليهم عمر ه ، رواه مسلم والبخاري ولنا ما روي من حديث العجلاني، = من خلافة عمر
The Book of Divorce. That is, in explanation of its rulings. It is the removal of the bond established legally through marriage. Divorcing her once in a pure state (tuhr) in which there was no intercourse, and leaving her. That is, divorce. That is, one divorce, attached to the subject. The Book of Divorce: [Linguistically, it is the removal of a bond absolutely, derived from releasing a camel, i.e., sending it from its hobble. It is a verbal noun meaning 'divorcing', like 'salam' meaning 'surrendering'. Legally, it is what the author mentioned. (Ayni, Musannaf)] The connection between the Book of Divorce and the Book of Breastfeeding: divorce is prohibited like breastfeeding. The connection between divorce and marriage is opposition and contrast. He prioritized breastfeeding because its prohibition is permanent, while divorce has a fixed term, and prioritizing the stronger is more sound. Performing divorce is permissible. Some people say: it is not permissible except for necessity, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Allah curses every frequent divorcer and frequent wife-taker', and he said: 'The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce', and he said: 'Do not divorce women except for open lewdness; Allah does not love those who often divorce and often take wives', and he said: 'Marry and do not divorce.' Our proof is Allah's statement: {And when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period} (65:1) and {There is no blame upon you if you divorce women} (2:236). This implies permissibility. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, divorced Hafsah, and the Companions used to divorce without any objection. (Ayni, Fath, Zaylai). Removal of the bond: its cause is the need for release when dispositions differ. Its condition is that the husband be legally responsible, even constructively like a drunkard, and that the woman be married or in a waiting period in which she is fit to be a place for divorce. Its ruling is the occurrence of separation, deferred by the expiry of the waiting period in a revocable divorce, and immediate in an irrevocable divorce. Its pillar is the utterance itself. Its description is permissibility to rid oneself of religious and worldly dislikes, and it is the most detestable of permissible things. Its authority is given to the man because he is the owner, like one who acquires her through the mahr, and because she has no deliberation in her affairs. The number of it is legislated to enable reconsideration upon regret, and it is limited to three because it is a number fixed in law, and it is the smallest plural; there is no maximum to its greater number. Divorce is recommended if she is harmful or abandons prayer, and obligatory if retaining her with kindness is not possible, as in the case of one who hates her and the impotent man. It is prohibited if the divorce is bid'i (innovative). (Ayni, Fath). Legally: excludes the removal of a bond established physically, i.e., untying a rope. By marriage: excludes emancipation, because it is the removal of a bond legally established but not through marriage. (Ayni). Divorcing her etc.: [Raised as the subject, a verbal noun attached to the object, its implied construction: the man divorcing his wife is the subject, and 'ahsan' (best) is its predicate, meaning the best form of divorce is that the man divorces his wife with one divorce in a pure state (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her nor in the preceding menstruation, and leaves her until her waiting period expires. This category is better than 'hasan' (good) because there is no disagreement about the absence of dislike (karaha) in it, unlike 'hasan', for which Malik says there is dislike. The meaning of it being better is relative to the other part, not that it is good in itself; how can it be good in itself when it is the most detestable of permissible things? This is one of the two types of sunnah divorce: the sunnah divorce is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of 'sunnah' and 'sunni' here is that it is established in a manner that does not incur blame, not that it is followed by reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself. (Musaffa, Fath). And 'leaving her' in the nominative is a conjunction to the subject attached to the object, the agent is omitted, i.e., this divorcer leaves his wife. (Ayni). Sections of Divorce and Their Rulings. ...until her waiting period expires is 'ahsan' (best). And three in pure states is 'hasan' (good) and 'sunni' (according to Sunnah). And three in one pure state or by one word is 'bid'i' (innovative). That is, until she completes it: 'ahsan' is the predicate of the subject; because it was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions used to prefer not to increase divorce beyond one until her waiting period expires, and because it is farthest from regret due to enabling reconsideration. (Ayni). Pure states: i.e., divorcing her with three separate divorces in three pure states without intercourse, one in each tuhr for the one who has been entered. (Talwi, Ayni). 'Hasan' and 'sunni': [regarding time and number. Then it was said: the first is to delay the pronouncement to the end of the tuhr to avoid prolonging the waiting period. The more apparent is to divorce her as soon as she becomes pure. (Talwi)] Meaning, the 'hasan' and 'sunni' divorce is to divorce her three times in three pure states. And if 'hasan' is sunni, then it follows that 'ahsan' is sunni. Know that Sunnah in divorce is of two types: Sunnah in time, and Sunnah in number. The Sunnah in time is only established for the one who has been entered, and it is to divorce her once in a pure state in which he has not had intercourse with her, as passed. The Sunnah in number applies equally to the one who has been entered and the one who has not, because the Sunnah in number is to divorce her once. If it is in the one who has been entered in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in both number and time. If it is not in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in number and bid'i in time. If one divorces the one not entered once, it occurs as sunni whether in menstruation or purity, because desire for her is renewed in every state, unlike the one entered, because the time of menstruation is a time of aversion from her, and also because once intercourse in a tuhr reduces desire for her. Malik said: divorcing three times in pure states is bid'a because divorce is prohibited, so one should not proceed except to fulfill a need, which is achieved with one. Our proof: his statement, peace be upon him, to Umar: 'Order your son to take her back, then leave her until she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her, then she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her if he wishes.' And he said, peace be upon him: 'It is from the Sunnah to approach the pure state directly, and divorce her with each period a divorce.' (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni). And three: i.e., divorcing her three separate times in one pure state (Talwi) or by one word, by saying: 'You are divorced thrice' in a tuhr, or combining two divorces in a tuhr by one word or two words without a revocation in between. (Talwi, Ayni). Bid'i: [regarding number, sunni regarding time if the tuhr is free from intercourse. (Talwi, Ayni)] i.e., attributed to innovation regarding number; due to the narration of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, what if I divorced her three times? He said: 'Then you would have disobeyed your Lord, and she would be irrevocably separated from you.' Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah and al-Daraqutni. The meaning of his statement 'three in a tuhr' is that no revocation occurs between the two divorces; if revocation occurs, it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. If remarriage occurs between them, it is not disliked by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: Three divorces in one tuhr or by one word are not bid'a because divorce is legislated, and legislation is not compatible with prohibition, unlike divorce during menstruation, because the prohibited thing is prolonging the waiting period, not divorce. The proof against him is what we have narrated. So if he divorces three times in a tuhr or by one word, the divorce occurs and he becomes sinful. A group, including the Zahiris and Shi'ah, hold that three divorces together only count as one, due to the narration from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: Divorce was one at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and Abu Bakr, and two years of Umar's caliphate, then Umar enforced it as three. Reported by Muslim and al-Bukhari. Our proof is the narration from the 'Ujlayni hadith, = from the caliphate of Umar.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Talaq with a comprehensive definition and classification. The author defines divorce (talaq) as the removal of the marriage bond established by shari'ah. Linguistically, it is derived from releasing a camel from its hobble; legally, it is as the author states. The placement of Talaq after the book of Radha' (breastfeeding) is justified: both involve prohibition, but divorce is temporary while radha' is permanent, so the stronger is placed first. The ruling on divorce is ibahah (permissibility), though there is a minority view that it is only for necessity, citing hadiths that condemn divorce. The Hanafi position relies on clear Quranic verses (65:1 and 2:236) that imply permission, the Prophet's own divorce of Hafsah, and the general practice of the Companions without censure. Divorce is the most detestable of permissible things (abghadh al-mubahat). Its cause is the need for relief when spouses are incompatible; its condition for the husband is legal responsibility (taklif) even constructively for a drunkard; for the wife, she must be married or in a revocable waiting period; its ruling is the occurrence of separation (firqah), deferred in revocable divorce (raj'i) until iddah ends, immediate in irrevocable (ba'in); its pillar (rukn) is the utterance itself. The number of pronouncements is limited to three because it is a legally fixed number and the smallest plural; there is no maximum number of three. Divorce is recommended (mustahabb) if the wife is harmful or neglects prayer; obligatory (wajib) if retaining her with kindness is impossible, as in cases of extreme aversion or impotence; and prohibited (haram) if it is bid'i (innovative). The passage then details the three categories of divorce based on time and number: Ahsan (best): one pronouncement in a tuhr (pure period) with no intercourse, followed by leaving her to complete her iddah. This is agreed upon without dislike. Hasan (good): three pronouncements in three separate tuhrs. This is sunnah in time and number, though Imam Malik considers it disliked. Bid'i (innovative): three pronouncements in one tuhr (either separately without revocation in between) or by a single phrase. This is sinful (ma'siyah) but the divorce takes effect. Al-Shafi'i argues this is not bid'i because divorce is legislated and legislation cannot combine with prohibition; the Hanafi response cites the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet said three divorces in one tuhr make her irrevocable and constitute disobedience. The passage also notes that some (Zahiris, Shi'ah) hold that triple divorce counts as one, relying on the practice of the early caliphate, but the Hanafis reject this with other narrations. The teacher should emphasize that while divorce is permitted, it is most disliked, and the sunnah methods (ahsan and hasan) are prescribed to allow opportunity for reconciliation. The bid'i method is sinful yet effective—a critical distinction in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
أحسن (ahsan): The best form of divorce: one pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse, followed by leaving the wife to complete her iddah.
حسن (hasan): Good divorce: three pronouncements in three separate tuhrs.
بدعي (bid'i): Innovative divorce: three pronouncements in one tuhr or by one word. It is sinful but effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, which of the following is true about the 'hasan' (good) divorce?
A) It is considered bid'a by all scholars.
B) It is three divorces in three separate pure states, and it is sunnah.
C) It is the same as ahsan.
D) It is prohibited because it involves three pronouncements.

Key Takeaway
Divorce falls into three categories based on time and number: the best (ahsan) uses one pronouncement in a pure state, the good (hasan) uses three in separate pure states, and the innovative (bid‘i) uses three at once – all are valid but vary in sin.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
The Dispute on Triple Divorce in One Sitting (Bid‘i)
Inter-madhhab dispute on triple divorce in one tuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on triple divorce in one tuhr or by one word, contrast it with the Shafi‘i and Zahiri views, and evaluate the proofs used by each side.

Core Idea
Triple divorce in one sitting is bid‘i, sinful, but counts as three – a view supported by explicit hadith against Shafi‘i’s logical objection.

One of the most debated issues in divorce law is whether pronouncing three divorces at once (or in one pure period) counts as three or one, and whether it is sinful. The Hanafi school takes a strong stance: it is bid‘i (innovative), the husband disobeys Allah, but the divorce takes effect as three, making the wife irrevocably separated. This lesson dissects the inter-madhhab dispute, examining the proof from Ibn Umar’s hadith and the counterarguments from al-Shafi‘i and the Zahiris/Shi‘ah.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi ruling: if a man says 'You are divorced thrice' in one tuhr (or by separate statements without revocation), the divorce counts as three, and he becomes sinful (asi). The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet said that three divorces in one sitting constitute disobedience and make the wife irrevocable.
The passage also notes that if the husband revokes (returns) between two divorces, it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa.
2
2. Understand the Shafi‘i objection
Al-Shafi‘i argues that triple divorce in one tuhr is not bid‘i because divorce is legislated (mashru‘) and legislation cannot combine with prohibition (hazr). He distinguishes it from divorce during menstruation: there the prohibition is about prolonging iddah, not the divorce itself.
Shafi‘i thus holds it is valid without sin, though still three divorces.
3
3. Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis respond with the explicit hadith: the Prophet called it disobedience (asi). The prohibition is on the manner (kayfiyyah) – going against the sunnah – not on the essence of divorce. Something can be valid and sinful simultaneously (e.g., fasting on Eid).
This is a key usul principle: validity and sin can coexist when the prohibition is external to the act's essence.
4
4. Consider the Zahiri/Shi‘i view
A group (Zahiris, Shi‘ah) holds that triple divorce in one sitting counts as one divorce, relying on the practice of the early caliphate where divorce was one until ‘Umar enforced it as three.
The Hanafi response is the hadith of ‘Ujlayni (mentioned briefly) and the fact that the Companions accepted ‘Umar’s enforcement.

هو رفع القيد الثابت شرعاً بالنكاح؛ تطليقها واحدةً في طهر لا وطئ فيه، وتركها

أي طلقة واحدة متعلق بالمبتدأ
كتاب الطلاق: [هو لغة رفع القيد مطلقاً مأخوذ من إطلاق البعير وهو إرساله . من عقاله، ومصدر بمعنى التطليق كالسلام بمعنى التسليم وشرعا ما ذكره المصنف. (ع ، مس] المناسبة بين كتاب الطلاق وكتاب الرضاع: أن الطلاق محرم كالرضاع، والمناسبة بين الطلاق والنكاح التقابل والتضاد، وقدم الرضاع؛ لأن حرمته مؤبدة، والطلاق مغيا بغاية، وتقديم الأشد أسد، وإيقاع الطلاق مباح، ومن الناس من يقول: لا يباح إلا للضرورة؛ لقوله عليه: "لعن الله كل ذواق مطلاق"، وقال له: "أبغض الحلال إلى الله تعالى الطلاق، وقال: لا تطلقوا النساء إلا من ربيبة إن الله لا يحب الذواقين ولا الذواقات، وقال: زوجوا ولا تطلقوا، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِّقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ (الطلاق: 1) وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ ﴾ (البقرة : ٢٣٦) هذا يقتضي الإباحة، وطلق رسول الله الله ، حفصة، والصحابة كانوا يطلقون من غير نكير. ( عيني، فتح، زيلعي) رفع القيد: وسببه الحاجة إلى الخلاص عند تباين الأخلاق وشرطه كون الزوج مكلفاً ولو تقديراً كسكران، وكون المرأة منكوحة أو في عدة تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق، وحكمه وقوع الفرقة مؤجلاً بانقضاء العدة في الرجعي، وبدونه في البائن، وركنه نفس اللفظ، ووصفه الإباحة للتخلص به من المكاره الدينية والدنيوية، وهو أبغض المباحات وجعلت ولايته إلى الرجل؛ لأنه المالك كالمسترق لها بالمهر؛ ولأنها لا روية لها في أمورها، و شرع ا العدد فيه للتمكن من التدارك عند الندم وانحصر في الثلاث؛ لأنه عدد متعين في الشرع، وهو أقل الجمع؛ ولا نهاية لأكثره، ويستحب الطلاق لو مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة، ويجب لو فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في المحبوب والعنين، ويحرم لو كان الطلاق بدعياً. (عيني، فتح)
شرعاً: احترز به عن رفع القيد الثابت حساً وهو حل الوثاق. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣١/١] بالنكاح احترز به عن العتق؛ لأنه رفع قيد ثابت شرعا لكنه لا بالنكاح (ع) تطليقها إلخ: [مرفوع بالابتداء، مصدر مضاف إلى المفعول تقديره تطليق الرجل امرأته مبتدأ، وأحسن خبره أي أحسن الطلاق يطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه ولا في الحيض الذي قبله ويتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها، وإنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الحسن؛ لأنه لا خلاف لأحد في عدم الكراهة فيه بخلاف الحسن، فإن مالكاً يقول فيه بالكراهة، ومعنى كونه أحسن أي بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن، وكيف يكون حسناً في نفسه مع أنه أبغض المباح، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون؛ فإن الطلاق المسنون حسن وأحسن، ومعنى المسنون والسني هنا أنه ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المتعقب للثواب؛ لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه. (مص، فتح) وتركها بالرفع عطف على المبتدأ مضاف إلى المفعول والفاعل متروك أي وترك هذا المطلق امرأته. (ع)

حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن، وثلاثاً في أطهار حسن وسنّي، وثلاثاً في طهر أو بكلمةٍ بدعي
أي إلى أن تنقضي أحسن: خبر المبتدأ؛ لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أن الصحابة كانوا يستحبون أن لا يزيدوا في الطلاق على واحدة حتى تمضي عدتها؛ ولأنه أبعد من الندم لتمكنه من التدارك. (ع)
:
أطهار أي تطليقها ثلاث طلقات متفرقة في ثلاثة أطهار لا وطء فيها في كل طهر واحد للمدخول بها. (ط، ع) حسن وسني: [من حيث الوقت والعدد ثم قيل: الأولى أن يؤخر الإيقاع إلى آخر وقت الطهر احترازا عن تطويل العدة، والأظهر أن يطلقها كما طهرت (ط)] يعني الطلاق الحسن والسني أن يطلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار، وإذا كان الحسن سنياً فلأن يكون الأحسن سنياً بالأولى. واعلم أن السنة في الطلاق على نوعين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد. فالسنة في الوقت لا يثبت إلا بالمدخول بها خاصة وهو أن يطلقها واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه كما مر والسنة في العدد يستوي فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها؛ لأن السنة في العدد هو أن يطلقها واحدة فإن كانت في الموطوءة في طهر خال عن الجماع يكون سنياً في العدد والوقت.
وإن لم يكن في طهر خال عن الجماع وهو سني في العدد وبدعي في الوقت، وإذا طلق غير المدخول بها واحدة يقع سنيا سواء كان في الحيض أو الطهر؛ لأن الرغبة متجددة فيها على كل حال، بخلاف الموطوءة؛ لأن زمان الحيض زمان النفرة عنها، وأيضاً بالجماع مرة في طهر تقل الرغبة إليها، وقال مالك: التطليق ثلاثاً في أطهار بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق محظور فلا يباح الإقدام عليه إلا لدفع الحاجة وهو يحصل بالواحدة ولنا: قوله عليه لعمر ه: مر ابنك فليراجعها، ثم يدعها حتى تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها ثم تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها إن أحب"، وقال عليها: "إن من السنة أن يستقبل الطهر استقبالاً فيطلقها بكل قرء تطليقة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وثلاثاً : أي تطليقها ثلاثاً متفرقة في طهر واحد (ط) أو بكلمة واحدة بأن قال: أنت طالق ثلاثاً في طهر، أو جمع بين التطليقتين في طهر بكلمة أو بكلمتين لم يتخلل بينهما رجعة. (ط،ع) بدعي: [من . حيث العدد سني من حيث الوقت إن خلا الطهر عن الجماع. (ط، ع)] أي منسوب إلى البدعة من حيث العدد؛ لما روي في حديث ابن عمر له قال : قلت: يا رسول الله ! أرأيت لو طلقتها ثلاثاً؟" قال: "إذا قد عصيت ربك وبانت منك امرأتك"، رواه ابن أبي شيبة والدار قطني، والمراد بقوله: "ثلاثاً في طهر" أنه لم يتخلل بين التطليقتين رجعة وإن تخلل فلا يكره عند أبي حنيفة رحاله ، وإن تخلل التزوج بينهما فلا يكره بالإجماع، وقال الشافعي: لا تكون الثلاث في طهر واحد أو في كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق مشروع، والمشروعية لا يجامع الحظر بخلاف الطلاق في حالة الحيض؛ لأن الحرام تطويل العدة لا الطلاق والحجة عليه ما روينا، فإذا طلق ثلاثا في طهر أو بكلمة وقع الطلاق وصار عاصياً، وذهب جماعة منهم الظاهرية والشيعة إلى أن الطلاق الثلاث جملة لا تقع إلا واحدة؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه قال: كان الطلاق على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر، وسنتين ما واحدة فأمضاه عليهم عمر ه ، رواه مسلم والبخاري ولنا ما روي من حديث العجلاني، = من خلافة عمر
The Book of Divorce. That is, in explanation of its rulings. It is the removal of the bond established legally through marriage. Divorcing her once in a pure state (tuhr) in which there was no intercourse, and leaving her. That is, divorce. That is, one divorce, attached to the subject. The Book of Divorce: [Linguistically, it is the removal of a bond absolutely, derived from releasing a camel, i.e., sending it from its hobble. It is a verbal noun meaning 'divorcing', like 'salam' meaning 'surrendering'. Legally, it is what the author mentioned. (Ayni, Musannaf)] The connection between the Book of Divorce and the Book of Breastfeeding: divorce is prohibited like breastfeeding. The connection between divorce and marriage is opposition and contrast. He prioritized breastfeeding because its prohibition is permanent, while divorce has a fixed term, and prioritizing the stronger is more sound. Performing divorce is permissible. Some people say: it is not permissible except for necessity, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Allah curses every frequent divorcer and frequent wife-taker', and he said: 'The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce', and he said: 'Do not divorce women except for open lewdness; Allah does not love those who often divorce and often take wives', and he said: 'Marry and do not divorce.' Our proof is Allah's statement: {And when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period} (65:1) and {There is no blame upon you if you divorce women} (2:236). This implies permissibility. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, divorced Hafsah, and the Companions used to divorce without any objection. (Ayni, Fath, Zaylai). Removal of the bond: its cause is the need for release when dispositions differ. Its condition is that the husband be legally responsible, even constructively like a drunkard, and that the woman be married or in a waiting period in which she is fit to be a place for divorce. Its ruling is the occurrence of separation, deferred by the expiry of the waiting period in a revocable divorce, and immediate in an irrevocable divorce. Its pillar is the utterance itself. Its description is permissibility to rid oneself of religious and worldly dislikes, and it is the most detestable of permissible things. Its authority is given to the man because he is the owner, like one who acquires her through the mahr, and because she has no deliberation in her affairs. The number of it is legislated to enable reconsideration upon regret, and it is limited to three because it is a number fixed in law, and it is the smallest plural; there is no maximum to its greater number. Divorce is recommended if she is harmful or abandons prayer, and obligatory if retaining her with kindness is not possible, as in the case of one who hates her and the impotent man. It is prohibited if the divorce is bid'i (innovative). (Ayni, Fath). Legally: excludes the removal of a bond established physically, i.e., untying a rope. By marriage: excludes emancipation, because it is the removal of a bond legally established but not through marriage. (Ayni). Divorcing her etc.: [Raised as the subject, a verbal noun attached to the object, its implied construction: the man divorcing his wife is the subject, and 'ahsan' (best) is its predicate, meaning the best form of divorce is that the man divorces his wife with one divorce in a pure state (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her nor in the preceding menstruation, and leaves her until her waiting period expires. This category is better than 'hasan' (good) because there is no disagreement about the absence of dislike (karaha) in it, unlike 'hasan', for which Malik says there is dislike. The meaning of it being better is relative to the other part, not that it is good in itself; how can it be good in itself when it is the most detestable of permissible things? This is one of the two types of sunnah divorce: the sunnah divorce is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of 'sunnah' and 'sunni' here is that it is established in a manner that does not incur blame, not that it is followed by reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself. (Musaffa, Fath). And 'leaving her' in the nominative is a conjunction to the subject attached to the object, the agent is omitted, i.e., this divorcer leaves his wife. (Ayni). Sections of Divorce and Their Rulings. ...until her waiting period expires is 'ahsan' (best). And three in pure states is 'hasan' (good) and 'sunni' (according to Sunnah). And three in one pure state or by one word is 'bid'i' (innovative). That is, until she completes it: 'ahsan' is the predicate of the subject; because it was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions used to prefer not to increase divorce beyond one until her waiting period expires, and because it is farthest from regret due to enabling reconsideration. (Ayni). Pure states: i.e., divorcing her with three separate divorces in three pure states without intercourse, one in each tuhr for the one who has been entered. (Talwi, Ayni). 'Hasan' and 'sunni': [regarding time and number. Then it was said: the first is to delay the pronouncement to the end of the tuhr to avoid prolonging the waiting period. The more apparent is to divorce her as soon as she becomes pure. (Talwi)] Meaning, the 'hasan' and 'sunni' divorce is to divorce her three times in three pure states. And if 'hasan' is sunni, then it follows that 'ahsan' is sunni. Know that Sunnah in divorce is of two types: Sunnah in time, and Sunnah in number. The Sunnah in time is only established for the one who has been entered, and it is to divorce her once in a pure state in which he has not had intercourse with her, as passed. The Sunnah in number applies equally to the one who has been entered and the one who has not, because the Sunnah in number is to divorce her once. If it is in the one who has been entered in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in both number and time. If it is not in a pure state free from intercourse, it is sunni in number and bid'i in time. If one divorces the one not entered once, it occurs as sunni whether in menstruation or purity, because desire for her is renewed in every state, unlike the one entered, because the time of menstruation is a time of aversion from her, and also because once intercourse in a tuhr reduces desire for her. Malik said: divorcing three times in pure states is bid'a because divorce is prohibited, so one should not proceed except to fulfill a need, which is achieved with one. Our proof: his statement, peace be upon him, to Umar: 'Order your son to take her back, then leave her until she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her, then she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her if he wishes.' And he said, peace be upon him: 'It is from the Sunnah to approach the pure state directly, and divorce her with each period a divorce.' (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni). And three: i.e., divorcing her three separate times in one pure state (Talwi) or by one word, by saying: 'You are divorced thrice' in a tuhr, or combining two divorces in a tuhr by one word or two words without a revocation in between. (Talwi, Ayni). Bid'i: [regarding number, sunni regarding time if the tuhr is free from intercourse. (Talwi, Ayni)] i.e., attributed to innovation regarding number; due to the narration of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, what if I divorced her three times? He said: 'Then you would have disobeyed your Lord, and she would be irrevocably separated from you.' Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah and al-Daraqutni. The meaning of his statement 'three in a tuhr' is that no revocation occurs between the two divorces; if revocation occurs, it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. If remarriage occurs between them, it is not disliked by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: Three divorces in one tuhr or by one word are not bid'a because divorce is legislated, and legislation is not compatible with prohibition, unlike divorce during menstruation, because the prohibited thing is prolonging the waiting period, not divorce. The proof against him is what we have narrated. So if he divorces three times in a tuhr or by one word, the divorce occurs and he becomes sinful. A group, including the Zahiris and Shi'ah, hold that three divorces together only count as one, due to the narration from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: Divorce was one at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and Abu Bakr, and two years of Umar's caliphate, then Umar enforced it as three. Reported by Muslim and al-Bukhari. Our proof is the narration from the 'Ujlayni hadith, = from the caliphate of Umar.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Talaq with a comprehensive definition and classification. The author defines divorce (talaq) as the removal of the marriage bond established by shari'ah. Linguistically, it is derived from releasing a camel from its hobble; legally, it is as the author states. The placement of Talaq after the book of Radha' (breastfeeding) is justified: both involve prohibition, but divorce is temporary while radha' is permanent, so the stronger is placed first. The ruling on divorce is ibahah (permissibility), though there is a minority view that it is only for necessity, citing hadiths that condemn divorce. The Hanafi position relies on clear Quranic verses (65:1 and 2:236) that imply permission, the Prophet's own divorce of Hafsah, and the general practice of the Companions without censure. Divorce is the most detestable of permissible things (abghadh al-mubahat). Its cause is the need for relief when spouses are incompatible; its condition for the husband is legal responsibility (taklif) even constructively for a drunkard; for the wife, she must be married or in a revocable waiting period; its ruling is the occurrence of separation (firqah), deferred in revocable divorce (raj'i) until iddah ends, immediate in irrevocable (ba'in); its pillar (rukn) is the utterance itself. The number of pronouncements is limited to three because it is a legally fixed number and the smallest plural; there is no maximum number of three. Divorce is recommended (mustahabb) if the wife is harmful or neglects prayer; obligatory (wajib) if retaining her with kindness is impossible, as in cases of extreme aversion or impotence; and prohibited (haram) if it is bid'i (innovative). The passage then details the three categories of divorce based on time and number: Ahsan (best): one pronouncement in a tuhr (pure period) with no intercourse, followed by leaving her to complete her iddah. This is agreed upon without dislike. Hasan (good): three pronouncements in three separate tuhrs. This is sunnah in time and number, though Imam Malik considers it disliked. Bid'i (innovative): three pronouncements in one tuhr (either separately without revocation in between) or by a single phrase. This is sinful (ma'siyah) but the divorce takes effect. Al-Shafi'i argues this is not bid'i because divorce is legislated and legislation cannot combine with prohibition; the Hanafi response cites the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet said three divorces in one tuhr make her irrevocable and constitute disobedience. The passage also notes that some (Zahiris, Shi'ah) hold that triple divorce counts as one, relying on the practice of the early caliphate, but the Hanafis reject this with other narrations. The teacher should emphasize that while divorce is permitted, it is most disliked, and the sunnah methods (ahsan and hasan) are prescribed to allow opportunity for reconciliation. The bid'i method is sinful yet effective—a critical distinction in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
بدعي (bid'i): Innovative divorce: three pronouncements in one tuhr or by one word. It is sinful but effective.
عاصٍ (asi): Disobedient; one who commits a sin (ma'siyah).
اختلاف المشروعية والحظر (ikhtilaf al-mashru‘iyyah wa al-hazr): The Shafi‘i argument that a legislated act cannot be simultaneously prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a man who divorces his wife three times in one sitting is:
A) Not considered to have divorced at all because it is bid'a.
B) Has divorced her once only, following the practice of the early caliphate.
C) Has divorced her three times, and he is sinful.
D) Has divorced her three times, and there is no sin because divorce is permitted.

Key Takeaway
Triple divorce in one sitting is bid‘i and sinful, but it counts as three; the husband becomes a sinner and the wife is irrevocably separated.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Sunnah Divorce: Ahsan, Hasan, and the Maliki Objection
Defining types of sunnah divorce and rebutting Malik's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between ahsan, hasan, sunni, and bid'i divorce, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to Malik's claim that three divorces in three pure periods is bid'ah.

Core Idea
Three divorces in three pure periods is hasan, not bid'ah — the Hanafi school distinguishes sunnah in time from sunnah in number.

Divorce (talaq) in Islamic law is not a single uniform act. The Hanafi school categorizes divorces based on how and when they are pronounced. This lesson defines the four categories — ahsan, hasan, sunni, and bid'i — and addresses a direct challenge from Imam Malik, who considered any divorce beyond one to be bid'ah. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi methodology in weighing textual evidence (hadith) against apparent legal objectives (maqasid).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the three types of sunnah divorce: ahsan (one divorce, wait for iddah), hasan (three divorces in three pure periods), sunni (conforming to sunnah in time/number). Bid'i is three in one period or one word.
The author notes that hasan is also sunni, so ahsan is even more sunni.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik considers three in three periods bid'ah because divorce is prohibited except for need, and one divorce suffices.
Malik's reasoning: asl al-hazr (original ruling is prohibition).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik's proof is that the need for divorce is fulfilled by one pronouncement, so any excess is unnecessary and therefore bid'ah.
This is a qiyas on the principle of necessity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet instructed divorce in consecutive pure periods, showing that multiple divorces are permissible and even sunnah.
The hadith is cited: 'Tell your son to take her back, then leave her until she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her...'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis permit three in three periods (recommended), while Malikis consider it sinful. The fatwa in the Hanafi school follows the Hanafi position.
The difference affects the legal ruling for the husband.

أي إلى أن تنقضي أحسن: خبر المبتدأ؛ لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أن الصحابة كانوا يستحبون أن لا يزيدوا في الطلاق على واحدة حتى تمضي عدتها؛ ولأنه أبعد من الندم لتمكنه من التدارك. (ع)
:
أطهار أي تطليقها ثلاث طلقات متفرقة في ثلاثة أطهار لا وطء فيها في كل طهر واحد للمدخول بها. (ط، ع) حسن وسني: [من حيث الوقت والعدد ثم قيل: الأولى أن يؤخر الإيقاع إلى آخر وقت الطهر احترازا عن تطويل العدة، والأظهر أن يطلقها كما طهرت (ط)] يعني الطلاق الحسن والسني أن يطلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار، وإذا كان الحسن سنياً فلأن يكون الأحسن سنياً بالأولى. واعلم أن السنة في الطلاق على نوعين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد. فالسنة في الوقت لا يثبت إلا بالمدخول بها خاصة وهو أن يطلقها واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه كما مر والسنة في العدد يستوي فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها؛ لأن السنة في العدد هو أن يطلقها واحدة فإن كانت في الموطوءة في طهر خال عن الجماع يكون سنياً في العدد والوقت.
وإن لم يكن في طهر خال عن الجماع وهو سني في العدد وبدعي في الوقت، وإذا طلق غير المدخول بها واحدة يقع سنيا سواء كان في الحيض أو الطهر؛ لأن الرغبة متجددة فيها على كل حال، بخلاف الموطوءة؛ لأن زمان الحيض زمان النفرة عنها، وأيضاً بالجماع مرة في طهر تقل الرغبة إليها، وقال مالك: التطليق ثلاثاً في أطهار بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق محظور فلا يباح الإقدام عليه إلا لدفع الحاجة وهو يحصل بالواحدة ولنا: قوله عليه لعمر ه: مر ابنك فليراجعها، ثم يدعها حتى تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها ثم تحيض وتطهر ثم يطلقها إن أحب"، وقال عليها: "إن من السنة أن يستقبل الطهر استقبالاً فيطلقها بكل قرء تطليقة. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني)
Book of Divorce. Sections of Divorce and Their Rulings. So 'until her waiting period ends, that is better (ahsan), and three [divorces] in three pure periods is hasan and sunni, and three in one pure period or with one word is bid'i.' That is, 'until she ends' is better: predicate of the subject; because of what was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions used to prefer not to increase divorce beyond one until her waiting period ended; and because it is further from regret as he is able to remedy. (A) 'Pure periods': meaning divorcing her three separate divorces in three pure periods in which there is no intercourse in each pure period for the one who has been consummated. (T, A) 'Hasan and sunni': regarding time and number. Then it was said: the best is to delay the pronouncement to the end of the pure period to avoid lengthening the waiting period, but the more apparent is that he divorces her when she becomes pure. (T) Meaning hasan and sunni divorce is to divorce her three times in three pure periods. Since hasan is sunni, then ahsan is even more sunni. Know that the sunnah in divorce is of two types: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. Sunnah in time is only established for the consummated wife specifically, and it is that he divorces her once in a pure period in which he did not have intercourse with her, as previously mentioned. Sunnah in number applies equally to the consummated and non-consummated wife, because the sunnah in number is that he divorces her once. If that [one divorce] is for the consummated wife in a pure period free from intercourse, it is sunni in both number and time. If it is not in a pure period free from intercourse, it is sunni in number and bid'i in time. When he divorces the non-consummated wife once, it is sunni whether she is in menstruation or in a pure period, because desire is renewed for her in every state, contrary to the consummated wife, because the time of menstruation is a time of aversion from her, and also by having intercourse once in a pure period, desire for her decreases. Malik said: Divorcing three times in three pure periods is bid'ah, because divorce is prohibited, so one should not proceed with it except to fulfill a need, and that need is fulfilled by one divorce. Our proof: His statement to Umar: 'Tell your son to take her back, then leave her until she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her, then she menstruates and becomes pure, then divorce her if he wishes.' And he said: 'It is from the sunnah to face the pure period properly by divorcing her with each waiting period (qur') a divorce.' (Extracted, Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq defines the types of sunnah divorce (ahsan, hasan, sunni) and rebuts Imam Malik's claim that three divorces in three pure periods is bid'ah. The author begins by explaining that 'ahsan' (better) means to divorce once and wait until the waiting period ends, based on a narration from Ibrahim al-Nakhai and the reasoning that it leaves room for reconciliation. 'Hasan' and 'sunni' refer to divorcing three times in three separate pure periods, each without intercourse. The author then distinguishes sunnah in time (for consummated wives only) from sunnah in number (for all wives). If a woman is divorcing in a pure period free of intercourse, it is sunni in both time and number; otherwise, it is sunni in number but bid'i in time. For non-consummated wives, even divorcing during menstruation is sunni because desire remains. Imam Malik argued that any divorce beyond one is bid'ah, but the Hanafi school counters with the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet instructed divorce in consecutive pure periods. Thus, the Hanafi position is that three in three periods (with revocable divorces) is hasan and sunni, not bid'ah.

Key Terms
أحسن (ahsan): The best form: divorce once and then wait until the waiting period ends without remarrying.
حسن (hasan): Divorce three times in three pure periods without intercourse in between.
سني (sunni): Conforming to the sunnah in time and/or number.
بدعي (bid'i): Divorce that deviates from the sunnah, e.g., three in one period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of divorce is considered 'hasan'?
A) One divorce followed by waiting period
B) Three divorces in one sitting
C) Three divorces in three pure periods
D) One divorce during menstruation

Key Takeaway
Ahsan (one divorce, wait for iddah) is best; hasan (three in three pure periods) is praiseworthy and sunni; bid'i (three in one period) is sinful.

Triple Talaq in One Period: Bid'ah and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explaining bid'ah divorce and rebutting Shafi'i's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on triple talaq in one period, explain why it is considered bid'ah, and analyse the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Triple talaq in one period is bid'ah but effective – the sin is in the number, not the act.

This lesson tackles a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is pronouncing three divorces in a single pure period a sinful innovation? The Hanafi school rules that it is bid'ah and the husband becomes sinful, yet the divorces still take effect. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that because divorce is legislated, the prohibition cannot attach to the act itself. We will examine the proof texts and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: three divorces in one pure period or with one word is makruh tahrimi (sinful) and the divorces take effect. The husband becomes 'asi (disobedient).
Even though it is sinful, the divorce is legally valid.
2
Identify the opposing view (Shafi'i)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that triple talaq in one period is not bid'ah because the act of talaq itself is legislated; prohibition cannot coincide with legislation.
He analogises to divorce during menstruation, but distinguishes because the prohibition there is about prolonging iddah.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Examine the Shafi'i reasoning: talaq is mashru' (legislated), so labelling it bid'ah is contradictory. The only relevant prohibition is timing, not the number.
This is a usul argument about the nature of the command.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts with clear hadith evidence: the Prophet (ﷺ) told Ibn Umar that triple talaq constitutes disobedience. Legislation of the act does not preclude sinfulness when the manner is prohibited.
The hadith is explicit: 'If you divorce her three times, you have disobeyed your Lord.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: both schools agree the divorce is effective, but Hanafi deems the husband sinful, while Shafi'i does not. This affects the husband's moral and legal culpability.
The fatwa adopted by the Hanafi school is the position that the husband is sinful.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ط،ع) بدعي: [من . حيث العدد سني من حيث الوقت إن خلا الطهر عن الجماع. (ط، ع)] أي منسوب إلى البدعة من حيث العدد؛ لما روي في حديث ابن عمر له قال : قلت: يا رسول الله ! أرأيت لو طلقتها ثلاثاً؟" قال: "إذا قد عصيت ربك وبانت منك امرأتك"، رواه ابن أبي شيبة والدار قطني، والمراد بقوله: "ثلاثاً في طهر" أنه لم يتخلل بين التطليقتين رجعة وإن تخلل فلا يكره عند أبي حنيفة رحاله ، وإن تخلل التزوج بينهما فلا يكره بالإجماع، وقال الشافعي: لا تكون الثلاث في طهر واحد أو في كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأن الطلاق مشروع، والمشروعية لا يجامع الحظر بخلاف الطلاق في حالة الحيض؛ لأن الحرام تطويل العدة لا الطلاق والحجة عليه ما روينا، فإذا طلق ثلاثا في طهر أو بكلمة وقع الطلاق وصار عاصياً، وذهب جماعة منهم الظاهرية والشيعة إلى أن الطلاق الثلاث جملة لا تقع إلا واحدة؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه قال: كان الطلاق على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر، وسنتين ما واحدة فأمضاه عليهم عمر ه ، رواه مسلم والبخاري ولنا ما روي من حديث العجلاني، = من خلافة عمر - وفيه طلقها ثلاثاً قبل أن يأمره النبي الله (متفق عليه) و لم ينقل إنكاره، وحديث عائشة لها أن امرأة قالت: یا رسول الله ! إن رفاعة طلقني وبت طلاق (متفق عليه) و لم ينقل إنكاره، وقد روي وعلي وابن عمر له أجمعين، والجواب عن حديث ابن عباس لما أنه إنكار على من يخرج عن سنة الطلاق بإيقاع الثلاث، وإخبار عن تساهل الناس في مخالفة السنة في الزمان المتأخر عن العصرين كأنه قال: الطلاق الموقع الآن ثلاثاً كان في ذينك العصرين واحدة رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۲/۱] (مستخلص)
And 'three [in one period]': meaning divorcing her three separate times in one pure period (T) or with one word, such as saying 'You are thrice divorced' in a pure period, or combining two divorces in one period with one word or two words without revoking between them (T, A). 'Bid'i': [regarding number, sunni regarding time if the pure period is free from intercourse (T, A)] i.e., attributed to innovation (bid'ah) in terms of number because of what was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar: He said: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, do you think if I divorce her three times?' He said: 'Then you have disobeyed your Lord and your wife has become separated from you.' Narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba and al-Daraqutni. The meaning of 'three in a period' is that there is no revocability between the two divorces; if there is revocability, it is not disliked according to Abu Hanifa. If marriage intervenes between them, it is not disliked by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: Three divorces in one pure period or with one word is not bid'ah, because divorce is legislated and legislation does not coincide with prohibition, unlike divorce during menstruation, because what is forbidden is the lengthening of the waiting period, not the divorce itself. And the proof against him is what we narrated. So if he divorces three times in one period or with one word, the divorce occurs and he becomes sinful. A group including the Zahiris and Shi'a hold that triple divorce in one session only counts as one, because of what was narrated from Ibn Abbas that divorce during the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and two years of Umar's caliphate was one, and Umar made it three. This is narrated by Muslim and Bukhari. Our proof: the hadith of al-‘Ajlani from Umar's caliphate in which he divorced her three times before the Prophet ordered him, and his disapproval was not reported. And the hadith of Aisha that a woman said: 'O Messenger of Allah, indeed Rifa'a divorced me and irrevocably separated me' (agreed upon) and his disapproval was not reported. And it was narrated from Ali and Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them all. The response to Ibn Abbas's hadith is that it is a censure of those who deviate from the sunnah by pronouncing three divorces, and an explanation of people's negligence in later times. It is as if he said: 'The divorce now being executed as three was in those two eras only one.' (Rumuz al-Haqaiq 1:232, extracted)
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for three divorces pronounced in one pure period or with one word, which is considered bid'ah (innovative) in terms of number, unless there is revocability. Even if it is bid'ah, the divorce takes effect and the husband is sinful. The author rebuts Imam al-Shafi'i, who argued that triple divorce in one period is not bid'ah because the act of divorce itself is legislated, and the prohibition is only for lengthening the waiting period. The Hanafi response relies on hadith evidence, including the narration from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said such a person has disobeyed. The passage also refutes the opinion of Zahiris and Shi'is that triple divorce only counts as one, citing the hadith of al-‘Ajlani and the lack of disapproval from the Prophet. The famous hadith of Ibn Abbas is explained as a comment on the change in later practice, not as a ruling that triple divorce is ineffective.

Key Terms
بدعي (bid'i): An innovation; here, divorce that deviates from the sunnah in number (or time).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The divorce occurs three times; he has sinned.
D) The divorce is nullified.

Key Takeaway
Triple talaq in one period is sinful (bid'ah) but legally effective according to the Hanafi school.

Divorcing Non-Consummated and Non-Menstruating Wives: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on divorcing non-consummated and non-menstruating wives with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling on divorcing a non-consummated wife during menstruation and a non-menstruating woman immediately after intercourse, and explain Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response based on the distinction of ʿilla.

Core Idea
Divorce during menstruation is banned only for consummated wives; non-consummated and non-menstruating women are exempt because no ʿidda ambiguity exists.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq addresses two related issues: the permissibility of divorcing a non-consummated wife during her menstruation, and the timing of divorce for women who do not menstruate (minors, elderly, pregnant). The text presents the majority Hanafi view (zāhir al-riwāya) and then records the dissenting opinions of Zufar and, on the second issue, Muhammad. By studying this lesson, you will understand how the Hanafi school uses a specific ʿilla (effective cause) – the possibility of pregnancy and its effect on the ʿidda – to distinguish between cases that appear similar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of women
First, isolate the two distinct rulings: (1) divorcing a non-consummated wife (ghayr al-madkhūl bihā) during menstruation; (2) divorcing a woman who does not menstruate (lā taḥīḍ: minor, elderly, pregnant) immediately after intercourse. The Hanafi majority permits both; Zufar objects to both.
The text also mentions a secondary issue: spacing of divorces for non-menstruating women.
2
State Zufar's objection and his dalīl
Zufar argues that the natural aversion and legal prohibition (of divorce during menstruation) are the same whether the woman is consummated or not, so the rule should be identical. He cites the general wording of the hadith: 'Your son has missed the sunnah.'
Zufar's position is a qiyās khafī (hidden analogy) treating both cases as alike.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi majority responds by pointing out a key difference: the prohibition for a consummated wife is due to the possibility of pregnancy, which makes the ʿidda ambiguous. For a non-consummated wife, no such possibility exists, so the rationale (ʿilla) is absent. The hadith about Umar is specified to refer only to the consummated wife because the command to 'take her back' (muriājiʿaha) has no application to a non-consummated wife.
This is a taṣḥīḥ (specification) of the general hadith.
4
Extend the same principle to non-menstruating women
The same ʿilla (no possibility of pregnancy) applies to minors below nine, elderly women past fifty-five, and pregnant women (since pregnancy already exists). Therefore, immediate divorce is permissible without waiting for a month. Zufar again disagrees, arguing that the month stands in place of menstruation, but the majority holds that since pregnancy is not possible (or is already evident), no waiting is needed.
For pregnant women, Muhammad and Zufar say only one sunnī divorce is allowed; the majority permits more but considers it bidʿī if more than one.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamara al-khilāf)
The dispute changes the legal ruling: according to Zufar, a husband must wait until after menstruation (for non-consummated) or one month (for non-menstruating) to divorce; according to the majority, immediate divorce is valid and sunnī in number (if kept to one).
The muftā bihī in the Hanafi school is the majority view, as stated in the text as 'zāhir al-riwāya'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
