( لا تحيض: بصغر بأن لم تبلغ تسع سنين أو كبر بأن بلغت خمسا وخمسين أو حمل. (ط) وصح طلاقهن أي حل؛ لأن الكلام فيه لا في الصحة؛ لأن الكراهة في ذوات الحيض باعتبار توهم الحمل؛ لأن عند ذلك يشتبه وجه العدة ولم يوجد في من لا تحيض والمعنى أنه يجوز أن يطلق من لا تحيض ولا يفصل بين طلاقها ووطئها بزمان، وقال زفر يفصل بشهر ؛ لقيامه مقام الحيض في حقها؛ ولأن الجماع ينفر الرغبة ويتجدد الرغبة بالزمان، ولنا أنه لا يتوهم الحمل في حقها، والكراهة في ذوات الحيض باعتباره. She is divorced according to the sunnah, which is a single divorce, no more than that (T). Even if she is menstruating [connected: meaning even if the woman is menstruating, and this is the apparent narration (T)]. Zufar said: He should not divorce her during menstruation; because the natural aversion and legal prohibition are the same regardless of consummation, so it becomes like the consummated woman; and because of his statement to Umar: 'Indeed your son has missed the sunnah.' So consideration is given to the general wording. Our proof: desire does not diminish for the non-consummated wife whether she is menstruating or pure, so he achieves his purpose, unlike the consummated wife, for her pure period is the time of specific desire. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 1:233] And the hadith applied to the consummated woman, as indicated by the rest of the hadith, i.e., 'Let him take her back,' because revocation is not applicable to the non-consummated. (Extracted, Fath)
'And he should space out' – i.e., the husband should space out the divorces for the consummated wife according to the sunnah in terms of time and number. (T, A) Regarding the woman who does not menstruate, because the month stands in place of the menstrual period. Then if he pronounces it at the beginning of the month, meaning the first night when the crescent moon is seen, the months are calculated by lunar months by agreement. If it is in the middle, then by days when spacing out; so he should not pronounce the second on the day completing thirty days, but rather on the thirty-first. Similarly in the waiting period according to the Imam. Spacing out divorce over months for the woman who does not menstruate is hasan and sunni. According to Muhammad and Zufar: The pregnant woman is not divorced according to the sunnah except once, because the month for her is not part of the intervals of the waiting period, so she becomes like one with extended purity. Their proof: permission is due to need, and the month is evidence of it as in the case of the elderly and the minor, unlike the one with extended purity, because menstruation is hoped for in her case, but it is not hoped for with pregnancy. The husband may divorce the minor and the elderly immediately after intercourse. Zufar said: He should not divorce her immediately but after a month. As for the pregnant woman, if he pronounces it immediately after intercourse, it is permissible by consensus. (Ayni, Fath)
('Does not menstruate' includes) due to young age, i.e., not having reached nine years, or old age, i.e., reached fifty-five, or pregnancy. (T) 'And valid (in the margin: permissible)' because the discussion is about permissibility, not validity; for the dislike in menstruating women is due to the possibility of pregnancy, because then the period of the waiting period is ambiguous, and such possibility is absent in those who do not menstruate. The meaning is that it is permissible to divorce the woman who does not menstruate without separating between divorce and intercourse by any period. Zufar said: He should separate by a month, because it stands in place of menstruation for her, and because intercourse diminishes desire and desire is renewed by time. Our proof: pregnancy is not possible in her case, and the dislike in menstruating women is due to that possibility. (Fath, Mis) 'After intercourse': without separation, and it is bid'i in terms of number if it is more than one. (T, A)
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage covers three related issues: (1) Divorcing a non-consummated wife during menstruation: the Hanafi position, opposed by Zufar, holds it permissible because desire is not affected by menstruation. (2) Divorcing a woman who does not menstruate (minor, elderly, pregnant): the Hanafi view permits immediate divorce without waiting periods; Muhammad and Zufar restrict this, arguing the month substitutes for menstruation. (3) The ruling on divorcing immediately after intercourse for such women: it is permissible but if more than one divorce, it becomes bid'i. The passage also clarifies that the discussion is about permissibility, not validity, since validity is always assumed. The author concludes with Zufar's dissenting opinions and their rebuttals.

Key Terms
المدخول بها (al-madkhūl bihā): A woman with whom marriage has been consummated (sexual intercourse has taken place).
غير المدخول بها (ghayr al-madkhūl bihā): A woman with whom marriage has not been consummated.
لا تحيض (lā taḥīḍ): Women who do not menstruate: minors (under nine), elderly (over fifty-five), and pregnant women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the prohibition is only for consummated wives due to the possibility of pregnancy.
C) Because the hadith about Umar was not authentic.
D) Because the divorce is not valid anyway.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits divorcing a non-consummated wife at any time, including during menstruation, and allows immediate divorce for non-menstruating women, because the prohibition's rationale (possibility of pregnancy) is absent in these cases.

Talaq al-Sunnah for the Non-Entered Woman: Permissibility During Menstruation
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing a non-entered woman during menstruation, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar, and apply the evidence to distinguish the ruling from that of an entered woman.

Core Idea
A non-entered woman may be divorced during menstruation; her desire remains strong, so the prohibition for entered women does not apply.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific scenario in divorce law: the timing of talaq al-sunnah for a woman who has not been entered upon. While sunnah divorce generally requires a state of purity (tuhr) without intercourse, the Hanafi school makes an exception for ghayr al-mawtu'a. This lesson dissects the ruling, the evidence from hadith, and an internal Hanafi disagreement with Zufar, which hinges on the interpretation of natural aversion and legal impediment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage's opening statement: 'And the woman not entered upon is divorced according to the sunnah, even if she is menstruating.' Note that the act is talaq al-sunnah (one revocable divorce), the subject is ghayr al-mawtu'a, and the condition of purity is waived. Understand that this is an exception to the general rule.
The passage also clarifies the term 'those who do not menstruate' as young, elderly, or pregnant women.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The text cites two hadiths (Ibn Umar and Aisha) to show the Prophet did not disapprove of divorcing a non-entered woman during menstruation. The key reasoning: desire (raghbah) for the husband remains strong in a non-entered woman, whether she is menstruating or not, unlike an entered woman whose desire is tied to the time of purity. Thus, the prohibition due to extended waiting period does not apply.
The Hanafi response to Zufar's hadith argument is that the hadith about 'deviating from the sunnah' referred to an entered woman, as proven by the command to take her back (raj'ah), which is only for entered women.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
Zufar argues that natural aversion and legal prohibition are general and do not differ with entry, so the same prohibition applies. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) reply that for ghayr al-mawtu'a, desire is not diminished by menstruation, and the hadith's generality is restricted by its context. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: according to Zufar, divorcing during menses would be bid'ah; according to the majority, it is sunnah.
The text states the majority view is 'zahir al-riwaya' and thus mufta bihi.

The Book of Divorce: Sections of Divorce and Their Rulings: And the woman not entered upon is divorced according to the sunnah, even if she is menstruating, and it is distinguished by months for the one who does not menstruate, meaning she who has not been entered upon. = Meaning the young girl, the elderly woman, and the pregnant woman; that is textually from Umar. - And in it, he divorced her three times before the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered him (agreed upon) and his disapproval was not reported, and the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that a woman said: O Messenger of Allah! Indeed Rifa'a divorced me and made it final (agreed upon) and his disapproval was not reported, and it was narrated from Ali and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them all), and the response to the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) is that it is a disapproval of one who deviates from the sunnah of divorce by pronouncing three, and an informing about people's leniency in opposing the sunnah in a later time after the two eras; it is as if he said: the divorce pronounced now as three was in those two eras as one. (from Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:232, adapted). She is divorced according to the sunnah, and it is one divorce without any increase. (T) and even if she is menstruating [connected: meaning even if the woman is menstruating and that is the apparent narration (T)] and Zufar said: He should not divorce her in the state of menstruation because natural aversion and legal prohibition do not differ with or without entry, so she becomes like the entered upon; and because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed your son has deviated from the sunnah', so consideration is given to the generality of the wording. And our argument: desire is not weak for the non-entered upon, whether she is menstruating or pure, so that he can achieve his objective, unlike the entered upon, for her purity is the time of determined desire. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:233] and the hadith was about the entered upon, by indication of the rest of the hadith, which is his saying: 'Then let him take her back, for taking back does not occur in the non-entered upon.' (adapted, Fath).
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage begins the section on the categories of divorce and their rulings. It states the ruling that a woman who has not been entered upon (ghayr al-mawtu'a) is divorced according to the sunnah with a single divorce, and this is valid even if she is menstruating. The author then clarifies that 'those who do not menstruate' include the young girl, the elderly woman, and the pregnant woman. The text then engages in an intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar. Zufar argues that divorcing a non-entered woman during menstruation is not allowed because the prohibition due to natural aversion and legal impediment applies regardless of entry, and he cites the hadith 'Your son has deviated from the sunnah' generally. The Hanafi response is that desire remains strong for a non-entered woman even during menstruation, so the objection does not apply. The hadith about Ibn Umar was specific to an entered woman, as proven by the command to take her back, which is not applicable to a non-entered woman. Thus, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is permissible to divorce a non-entered woman during menstruation with one divorce.

Key Terms
الطلاق السنة (al-talaq al-sunnah): A divorce that conforms to the prophetic sunnah, which is a single revocable divorce pronounced in a woman's pure period without intercourse.
غير الموطوءة (ghayr al-mawtu'a): A woman with whom the husband has not had sexual intercourse.
بدعي (bid'ah): A divorce that is innovative and against the sunnah, such as pronouncing three divorces at once or divorcing during menstruation for an entered woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not permissible and is considered talaq al-bid'ah.
B) It is permissible and is considered talaq al-sunnah.
C) It is permissible only if the husband's purpose is to harm her.
D) It is permissible but only if she is pregnant.

Key Takeaway
A non-entered woman can be divorced with one revocable divorce during menstruation, and this is sunnah, not bid'ah, because her desire remains strong unlike an entered woman.

Divorcing Women Who Do Not Menstruate: Sunna and Permissibility
Ruling on sunnah divorce for non-menstruating women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of divorcing non-menstruating women and distinguish the ruling for pregnant women according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For non-menstruating women, the sunnah is one divorce per month; immediate divorce is permissible but not sunnah.

In the Hanafi school, the sunnah method of divorce involves timing and number. For women who do not menstruate (such as minors, the elderly, or pregnant women), the month replaces the menstrual period as a measure. This lesson explains the permissibility of immediate divorce and the preferred sunnah spacing, along with a key intra-Hanafi dispute on pregnant women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the women who do not menstruate
The text defines three categories: young girls (below nine), elderly women (above fifty-five), and pregnant women.
These women do not have menstrual periods to mark the iddah.
2
Understand the sunnah method
The sunnah is to pronounce one divorce at the start of a month (lunar) and then wait until the next month for the second, etc.
If the first divorce is in mid-month, count thirty days for the next.
3
Note the permissibility of immediate divorce
Despite the sunnah, it is legally permissible (ja'iz) to divorce these women immediately after intercourse; the text states this with consensus for the pregnant woman.
The disapproval for menstruating women is due to potential confusion in iddah, which does not apply here.
4
Analyze the dispute on the pregnant woman
Muhammad and Zufar argue that the month is not a phase of iddah for the pregnant woman, so only one sunnah divorce exists. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the month remains an indicator, so spreading over months is sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position follows the majority: the sunnah for all non-menstruating women, including the pregnant, is to space divorces over months.

And he distinguishes [i.e., the husband] the divorce, i.e., the divorce of the entered-upon woman according to the sunnah, in terms of time and number. (T, A) For she who does not menstruate, because the month in her case stands in place of the menstruation. Then, if he pronounces it at the beginning of the month, i.e., the first night when the crescent is seen, the months are calculated by lunar sighting (by agreement). And if in the middle, then by days in the separation, so he should not pronounce the second on the thirtieth day but on the thirty-first, and similarly in the iddah according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And spreading the divorce over months for one who does not menstruate is good and sunnah. And according to Muhammad and Zufar: the pregnant woman is not divorced according to the sunnah except with one, because the month in her case is not from the phases of the iddah, so she becomes like one with extended purity. And their argument: permissibility is due to the need, and the month is its indicator, as in the case of the elderly and young girl, unlike the one with extended purity; because menstruation is hoped for in her, but it is not hoped for during pregnancy. Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on divorcing women who do not menstruate, such as the young girl (below nine), the elderly (above fifty-five), and the pregnant. The key ruling is that it is permissible to divorce them immediately after intercourse without waiting, because the concern about confusing the iddah (which applies for menstruating women) does not arise. However, the sunnah method is to spread the divorce over months: one divorce per month, analogous to how menstruating women are divorced in each pure period. The text then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Imam Muhammad and Zufar, the pregnant woman should only be divorced with one divorce, not spread over months, because the month is not a phase of her iddah, unlike the young and elderly. However, the majority (Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the month serves as a measure of time for all such women. The text also notes a consensus that divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse is permissible. Finally, it clarifies that divorcing one who does not menstruate immediately after intercourse is permissible, but if one pronounces more than one divorce at once, it becomes bid'ah in terms of number.

Key Terms
من لا تحيض (man la tahid): Women who do not menstruate due to young age (below nine), old age (above fifty-five), or pregnancy.
تفريق الطلاق على الأشهر (tafriq al-talaq 'ala al-ashhur): Spreading the pronouncement of divorce over successive months, i.e., one divorce per month, which is the sunnah for non-menstruating women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Divorce her only in a pure period similar to menstruating women.

Key Takeaway
For non-menstruating women, the sunnah is to space divorce over months; immediate divorce is permissible but not sunnah, and the pregnant woman follows the same ruling according to the majority.

Bid'ah Divorce and the Second Pure Period: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling on bid'ah divorce and proper sunnah method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing an entered-upon wife during menstruation, explain why revocation is wajib, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the timing of the second pure period.

Core Idea
A bid'ah divorce is sinful but valid; the husband must revoke and then divorce in the second pure period.

Divorcing a woman with whom you have consummated the marriage is subject to strict sunnah timing. If a husband divorces her during her menstruation, he commits a sin (bid'ah), yet the divorce takes effect. The Shari'ah then requires him to revoke the divorce and wait for the correct moment to re-pronounce the talaq in accordance with the sunnah. The following passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains these rules, provides Quranic and Prophetic evidence, and reveals a subtle difference within the Hanafi school about what exactly constitutes the 'second pure period'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its primary ruling
The passage begins by describing the act of divorcing an entered-upon woman during her menstruation. Note that this is labeled 'bid'ah' (innovation) and the husband is termed 'disobedient' (asi). Confirm that the Hanafi school considers this divorce valid despite the sin.
Contrast with the Zahiri view mentioned later that such a divorce does not take effect.
2
Find the evidence (dalil) for the sinfulness and the obligation of revocation
Locate the Quranic verse (Surah al-Talaq 65:1) and the hadith of Ibn Umar (RA). The verse commands divorcing 'for their waiting period,' which implies purity. The hadith shows the Prophet (SAW) ordered Ibn Umar to take back his wife. Understand how this commands revocation.
The text says the correct view (asahh) is that revocation is wajib, not just recommended.
3
Understand the sunnah method after a bid'ah divorce
After revocation, the husband must wait and divorce in the 'second pure period'. Define what this means: she becomes pure from the menstruation in which divorce occurred, then menstruates again, then becomes pure again.
The passage presents two opinions within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa's view (first purity after divorce) vs. the Sahibayn's view (after a full cycle).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the second pure period
The text explicitly contrasts the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Note that the 'apparent narration' (zahir al-riwaya) is the Sahibayn's position. The matn (original text) is said to be the view of all three, but al-Tahawi reports a different narration from Abu Hanifa.
This is a rare case where the matn appears to adopt the Sahibayn's view, but a narration from Abu Hanifa differs.
5
Extend to triple talaq and cross-madhhab dispute
The passage concludes with the ruling on a man who says 'You are divorced' three times. The Hanafi school interprets this according to sunnah timing (one per pure period), while Shafi'i and Ahmad say all three occur immediately. Malik says only one falls.
This shows how usul principles (interpreting absolute utterances by sunnah) yield different outcomes across madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حائضاً بدعي فيراجعها ويُطلّقها في طهر ثان، ولو قال لموطوءته: أنت طالق عمر من حيث الوقت حائضا: أي التي دخل بها حال كونها حائضاً. (ع) بدعي: لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَطَلَقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ ﴾ (الطلاق: ١) أي لإظهار عدتهن، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام في حديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما لما أن طلق زوجته وهي حائض: "ما هكذا أمرنا الله تعالى" ولا خلاف في أنه بهذا الإيقاع عاص، ولما كان المنع منه في الحيض لتطويل العدة عليها كان النفاس كالحيض، وقوله: "فيراجعها" أي لدفع البدعة، والمراجعة قيل: مستحبة؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر عمر رضي الله عنه حيث قال: "مر ابنك" والأصح أنها واجبة عملا بحقيقة الأمر، ورفعا للمعصية بالقدر الممكن برفع أثره وهو العدة، ودفعا للضرر عنها بتطويل العدة، وقال أهل الظاهر : لا يقع الطلاق في الحيض؛ لأنه منهي عنه فلا يكون مشروعا ولنا ما روي في حديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما وكان قد طلقها في حالة الحيض: "مر ابنك فليراجعها؛ لأن المراجعة بدون وقوع الطلاق محال. (عيني، فتح) فيراجعها: وجوباً في الأصح لدفع البدعة. (ط) ويطلقها في طهر ثانٍ ذكر الطحاوي أنه يطلقها في الطهر الذي يلي الحيضة وهو قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وقولهما: أنها إذا طهرت من التي فيها الطلاق ثم حاضت ثم طهرت هو الطهر الثاني، لما رواه نافع عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه طلق امرأته وهي حائض، وفي رواية تطليقة على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: مره فليراجعها ثم يمسكها حتى تطهر وتحيض، ثم تطهر ثم إن شاء أمسك، وإن شاء أطلق قبل أن يمس فتلك العدة التي أمر الله أن تطلق لها النساء، رواه الجماعة غير ابن ماجه. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٣/١] ووجه ما ذكره الطحاوي من قول الإمام ما روى سالم عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه طلق امرأته وهي حائض فذكر ذلك عمر للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: "مره فليراجعها ثم ليطلقها إذا طهرت"، رواه مسلم والأربعة، والظاهر أن ما في الأصل قول الكل؛ لأنه موضوع لإثبات مذهب الإمام إلا أن يحكي الخلاف، ولم يحك فلهذا قال في الكافي: إنه ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة وما ذكره الطحاوي رواية عن أبي حنيفة. (فتح) طهر ثان أي إذا طهرت من تلك الحيضة التي وقع فيها الطلاق ثم حاضت ثم طهرت هو الطهر الثاني فيطلقها فيه في ظاهر الرواية وهو المذكور في الأصل. (ع) لموطوءته: أي حقيقة أو حكماً؛ لأن الخلوة كالدخول في حق مراعاة السنة، وقوله: "وقع عند كل طهر طلقة"؛ لأنه مطلق فيتناول الكامل هذا إذا لم ينو شيئاً، وكانت المرأة من ذوات الحيض، وإن كانت من ذوات الأشهر يقع في الحال طلقة، وبعد شهر أخرى، وبعد شهر آخر أخرى، وكذا الحامل إن لم يكن له نية أو نوى كذلك، وإن كان قبل الدخول بها وقعت للحال طلقة ثم لا يقع عليها قبل التزوج شيء؛ لأن تقدير هذا الكلام أنت طالق ثلاثاً لوقت السنة، فينصرف إلى السنة في حق كل واحدة منهن وعند الشافعي وأحمد في رواية في مسألة المتن: يقعن في الحال، وعند مالك واحدة والبائن ليس بسني في ظاهر الرواية؛ إذ لا حاجة إلى إثبات زيادة البينونة في الخلاص، والخلع سني سواء كان في حيض أو طهر؛ لأنه لا يمكن تحصيل البدل إلا به. (عيني، فتح)
(She is) menstruating, (the divorce is) bid'ah, so he must take her back and divorce her in a second pure period. And if he said to his entered-upon wife: 'You are divorced', by Umar regarding time, menstruating: i.e., she whom he has entered upon while she is menstruating. (A) Bid'ah: because of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So divorce them for their waiting period' (Al-Talaq 65:1), i.e., to show their waiting periods. And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said in the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) when he divorced his wife while she was menstruating: 'This is not how Allah commanded us.' And there is no disagreement that by this pronouncement he is disobedient. And since the prohibition during menstruation is to lengthen the waiting period upon her, postpartum bleeding is like menstruation. And his saying: 'He should take her back' is to repel the innovation. Taking back: it is said it is recommended because the Prophet commanded Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he said 'Order your son'. But the correct view is that it is obligatory, acting according to the reality of the command, and removing the disobedience as much as possible by removing its effect which is the waiting period, and repelling harm from her due to lengthening the waiting period. And the Zahiris said: the divorce does not take effect during menstruation because it is prohibited, so it cannot be legislated. Our proof: what is narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he had divorced her during menstruation: 'Order your son to take her back,' because taking back without the occurrence of divorce is impossible. (Ayni, Fath) He takes her back: obligatorily in the correct view to repel innovation. (T) And he divorces her in a second pure period. Al-Tahawi mentioned that he divorces her in the pure period that follows the (first) menstruation, and that is the saying of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). And their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) saying: that when she becomes pure from the one in which the divorce occurred, then menstruates, then becomes pure, that is the second pure period. Based on what Nafi' narrated from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating, and in a narration, one divorce during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Order him to take her back, then keep her until she becomes pure and menstruates, then becomes pure, then if he wishes he may keep her, and if he wishes he may divorce before touching. That is the waiting period which Allah commanded that women be divorced for.' Narrated by the group except Ibn Majah. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:233] And the justification of what al-Tahawi mentioned from the Imam is what Salim narrated from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating, and Umar mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Order him to take her back, then divorce her when she becomes pure.' Narrated by Muslim and the four (compilers). And the apparent meaning is that what is in the original (matn) is the saying of all, because it is intended to establish the Imam's madhhab unless it mentions disagreement, and it did not mention disagreement, so this is why it was said in al-Kafi: It is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa, and what al-Tahawi mentioned is a narration from Abu Hanifa. (Fath) Second pure period: i.e., when she becomes pure from that menstruation in which the divorce occurred, then menstruates, then becomes pure, that is the second pure period, and he divorces her in it in the apparent narration, and that is mentioned in the original. (A) For his entered-upon wife: i.e., actually or legally, because privacy is like entry in terms of observing the sunnah. And his saying: 'A divorce occurs at every pure period' because it is absolute and includes the completed one. This is when he did not intend anything, and the woman is one who menstruates. And if she is one of the months, one divorce occurs immediately, and another after a month, and another after another month. Similarly for the pregnant woman if he had no intention or he intended likewise. And if it was before entering upon her, one divorce occurs immediately, then nothing occurs before marriage. Because the estimation of this speech is: 'You are divorced three times for the time of the sunnah,' so it is directed to the sunnah for each of them. And according to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration regarding the issue of the text: they occur immediately. And according to Malik: one, and the irrevocable is not sunnah in the apparent narration, because there is no need to establish additional irrevocability in al-Khulasah. And khul' is sunnah whether in menstruation or purity, because the exchange cannot be obtained without it. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on divorcing a woman with whom intercourse has occurred (mawtu'a) during her menstruation. Such a divorce is bid'ah (innovation) and the husband becomes sinful. The correct sunnah method is to divorce her in a pure period without intercourse. If he has already committed the bid'ah divorce, he must revoke it (raj'a) and then divorce her in the second pure period (i.e., after she completes one full menstrual cycle following the divorce). The text presents evidence from the Quran (Surah al-Talaq) and the hadith of Ibn Umar. It then discusses a disagreement within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the second pure period is the one immediately following the menstruation in which the divorce occurred, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is after she menstruates again. The text sides with the Sahibayn as the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Finally, the passage explains the ruling on a man who says to his wife 'You are divorced' three times without specifying a time. According to the Hanafi school, it is interpreted according to the sunnah: if she is a menstruating woman, one divorce falls each pure period; if she is one who does not menstruate, one falls immediately and then after each month; and if before entry, one falls immediately. The text contrasts this with other schools: Shafi'i and Ahmad rule that all three fall immediately, Malik rules that one falls. The Hanafi position avoids immediate triple divorce, adhering to the sunnah method.

Key Terms
الطهر الثاني (al-tahr al-thani): The second pure period after the divorce in menstruation, which is when she becomes pure from the menstruation in which divorce occurred, then menstruates again, then becomes pure again.
بدعي (bid'ah): A divorce that is prohibited and against the sunnah, such as divorcing an entered-upon woman during menstruation or pronouncing three divorces at once.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the revocation (raj'a) after a bid'ah divorce?
A) It is recommended (mandub).
B) It is obligatory (wajib).
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is permissible (mubah).

Key Takeaway
A bid'ah divorce is sinful but valid; the husband must revoke it and then divorce in the second pure period, which, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, is after a full menstrual cycle.

Talaq — Divorce

The Ruling on Bid'i Divorce and the Obligation of Muraja'ah
Ruling with proof on bid'i divorce and muraja'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce during menstruation, explain why muraja'ah is wajib, and refute the Zahiri position.

Core Idea
A bid'i divorce is valid but sinful; muraja'ah is obligatory to remove the sin and rectify the harm.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on a divorce pronounced while the wife is menstruating (talaq bid'i). Although such a divorce is sinful, it is valid and takes effect. The husband is obligated to revoke it (muraja'ah) to shorten the 'iddah and eliminate the sin. We will explore the Quranic and hadith proofs and the reasoning behind making muraja'ah wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorcing a menstruating wife. It is haram (sinful) but the divorce itself is valid and takes effect. The husband is called 'asi (sinner).
2
Locate the dalil
Quran 65:1 ("Divorce them for their waiting period") implies divorce must be given at a time when the 'iddah can be properly counted. The hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet said "This is not how Allah commanded us" establishes the prohibition.
The hadith also includes the command to take her back, which is crucial for the next step.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic command 'for their waiting period' indicates that divorce should be given in a non-menstruating state so that the 'iddah is clear. The Prophet's rebuke confirms the act is prohibited. The prohibition is to prevent prolonging the 'iddah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Zahiris argue that a prohibited divorce does not occur at all. The Hanafi response: the Prophet ordered Ibn Umar to take her back, which presupposes the divorce actually happened.
This is a key point in Hanafi usul: prohibition does not necessarily invalidate the act itself.
5
Evaluate the position on muraja'ah
Muraja'ah is wajib according to the most correct view (al-asahh). The literal command and the goal of removing sin and shortening the 'iddah support obligation.
Some scholars considered it mustahabb, but the reliance is on the wajib view.

(ع) بدعي: لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَطَلَقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ ﴾ (الطلاق: ١) أي لإظهار عدتهن، وقال عليها في حديث ابن عمر ه لما أن طلق زوجته وهي حائض: "ما" هكذا أمرنا الله تعالى" ولا خلاف في أنه بهذا الإيقاع عاص، ولما كان المنع منه في الحيض لتطويل العدة عليها كان النفاس كالحيض، وقوله: "فيراجعها" أي لدفع البدعة، والمراجعة قيل: مستحبة؛ لأنه عليها أمر عمر الله حيث قال: "مر ابنك" والأصح أنها واجبة عملا بحقيقة الأمر، ورفعا للمعصية بالقدر الممكن برفع أثره وهو العدة، ودفعا للضرر عنها بتطويل العدة، وقال أهل الظاهر : لا يقع الطلاق في الحيض؛ لأنه منهي عنه فلا يكون مشروعا ولنا ما روي في حديث ابن عمر ما وكان قد طلقها في حالة الحيض: مر" ابنك فليراجعها؛ لأن المراجعة بدون وقوع الطلاق محال. (عيني، فتح) فيراجعها: وجوباً في الأصح لدفع البدعة. (ط)
Sections of divorce and their rulings. ['She is menstruating' is] a bid'i (innovative) divorce, so he should take her back and divorce her in a second purity. And if he said to his wife whom he has intercourse with: 'You are divorced'... [Commentary:] 'Menstruating': meaning one with whom he had intercourse while she was menstruating. 'Bid'i': because of His statement: 'Divorce them for their waiting period' (65:1), meaning to manifest their waiting periods. And the Prophet said in the hadith of Ibn Umar when he divorced his wife while she was menstruating: 'This is not how Allah commanded us.' There is no disagreement that by this occurrence he is sinful. And since the prohibition from it during menstruation is to lengthen the waiting period upon her, postpartum bleeding is like menstruation. And His statement: 'he should take her back' meaning to repel the innovation. Taking back (muraja'ah) is said to be recommended because the Prophet commanded Umar where he said: 'Order your son.' But the correct view is that it is obligatory, acting upon the literal meaning of the command, and to remove the sin as much as possible by removing its effect which is the waiting period, and to repel harm from her by lengthening the waiting period. The Zahiris said: divorce does not occur during menstruation because it is prohibited and thus not legitimate. Our proof is what was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar, when he had divorced her during menstruation: 'Order your son to take her back,' because taking back without the occurrence of divorce is impossible. (Ayni, Fath) 'He should take her back': obligation according to the most correct view to repel the innovation. (Tahawi)
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning divorce initiated during the wife's menstruation (talaq bid'i). The author first states the ruling: if a man divorces his menstruating wife, it is a bid'i divorce; he must revoke it (muraja'ah) and then divorce her in a subsequent pure period. The commentary explains that 'menstruating' means one with whom he had intercourse while she was menstruating, and 'bid'i' is derived from the Quranic verse (65:1) which commands divorcing for the 'iddah. The hadith of Ibn Umar establishes that such a divorce is sinful, as the Prophet said 'This is not how Allah commanded us.' The prohibition is to prevent prolonging the 'iddah. The commentary then addresses whether muraja'ah is obligatory or recommended; the stronger Hanafi position is that it is obligatory (wajib) to remove the sin and protect the wife from harm. The Zahiris argued that the divorce does not occur at all because it is prohibited, but the Hanafi response is that muraja'ah is only meaningful if the divorce actually occurred, as proven by the hadith.

Key Terms
بدعي (bid'i): A divorce that is innovated and contrary to the Sunnah, specifically when given during menstruation or postpartum bleeding.
مراجعة (muraja'ah): The act of taking back one's wife after a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) within the 'iddah period.
عاص (asi): Sinner; the person committing the prohibited act (here, divorcing during menstruation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is recommended (mustahabb)
B) It is obligatory (wajib)
C) It is prohibited (haram)
D) It is permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
An innovated divorce (bid'i) is valid but sinful; the husband must revoke it (muraja'ah) to eliminate the sin and protect the wife.

Timing of the Second Talaq: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of second talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on the timing of the second talaq after muraja'ah, identify the relied-upon view, and apply the correct timing in a given scenario.

Core Idea
The second talaq must wait until the second purity after the original divorce, not the first.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement on when exactly to give the second divorce after revoking the first. While both views come from within the school, the accepted position (zahir al-riwaya) is that of the two companions, requiring the husband to wait until the wife has menstruated and become pure again.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that this involves a bid'i talaq (given during menstruation) followed by muraja'ah (revocation). The question is: when should the second talaq be given to follow the Sunnah?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa holds that the second talaq is given in the first purity after the menstruation in which the original talaq was pronounced. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it must be given after the second purity (i.e., after another menstruation and subsequent purity).
The second purity means the state of purity after the next menses following the first purity.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Salim: 'Order him to take her back, then let him divorce her when she becomes pure.' The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Nafi': 'Keep her until she becomes pure and menstruates, then becomes pure.' Identify the operative phrase.
The Nafi' hadith explicitly mentions two purifications.
4
Determine the relied-upon view (tarjih)
The commentary notes that the position of the Sahibayn is the zahir al-riwaya (the standard transmission) and is mentioned in al-Asl. Therefore, the mufta bihi is the second purity view.
Zahir al-riwaya is the highest level of authority in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply to a concrete case
If a husband gives a first talaq during menstruation, revokes it before the menstruation ends, he must wait until she finishes that menstruation, then waits for the next menstruation and its subsequent purity. Only then should he give the second talaq.
Giving the second talaq earlier violates the sunnah timing but the talaq itself is still valid (though bid'i).

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the correct timing for the second divorce after a bid'i divorce. The text explains that after revoking the first divorce (muraja'ah), the husband should eventually give the second divorce in a 'second purity.' There are two views: Abu Hanifa holds that the second divorce should be given in the purity immediately following the menstruation in which the original divorce occurred (i.e., the first purity after that menstruation). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it should be given in the purity after the next menstruation (i.e., after she menstruates again and becomes pure). Both views rely on different hadith narrations from Ibn Umar. The commentary notes that the version in al-Asl (the original text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) is the statement of all (i.e., the companions agree with Abu Hanifa? Actually, it says the apparent position of al-Asl is the saying of all, but that is clarified as the zahir al-riwaya from Abu Hanifa. Al-Tahawi's narration is a separate narration. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) is that the second divorce is given after two purifications from the original divorce.

Key Terms
طهر ثانٍ (tuhur thanin): Second purity; the state of being free from menstruation after the next menses following the first purity.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted ruling from Imam Muhammad in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwaya, when should the second divorce be given after a bid'i talaq?
A) In the first purity after the original menstruation
B) In the second purity after the original menstruation (after another menses)
C) Immediately after muraja'ah
D) After the wife gives birth

Key Takeaway
The second talaq after muraja'ah should be given in the second purity (after another menstruation) according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Interpreting 'Three for the Sunnah': Timing and Intention
Interpretation of 'three for the sunnah' and intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of a husband saying 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' and distinguish the effect of his intention on the timing of the divorces.

Core Idea
Intentions can shape the timing of a 'three for the sunnah' divorce, but the wording must grammatically support the intended outcome.

In this lesson, we examine a specific expression used by husbands when pronouncing three divorces: 'You are divorced three for the sunnah.' The Hanafi school has detailed rules on how this expression is to be understood, considering the woman's menstrual status and the husband's intention. This passage also highlights a disagreement with Zufar regarding the validity of intending immediate triple divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its default operation
The phrase 'three for the sunnah' implies one divorce per purity or per month, depending on the woman's condition. Note the assumed scenario: no specific intention.
Default: one divorce at each purity if menstruating, or one per month if non-menstruating.
2
Analyze the effect of intention
If the husband intends the three to occur immediately, the Hanafi view is that his intention is valid because his wording can bear that meaning. Contrast with Zufar's objection that intention cannot contradict the sunnah.
Hanafi position: intention is valid; Zufar: not valid.
3
Determine the role of mentioning the number 'three'
The text explains that if the husband does not mention the number 'three' (e.g., just 'You are divorced for the sunnah'), the three divorces cannot occur together even by intention. The mention of 'three' is necessary for the possibility of immediate occurrence.
Mentioning 'three' is crucial for the intention of immediate triple divorce to be effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لموطوءته: أي حقيقة أو حكماً؛ لأن الخلوة كالدخول في حق مراعاة السنة، وقوله: "وقع عند كل طهر طلقة"؛ لأنه مطلق فيتناول الكامل هذا إذا لم ينو شيئاً، وكانت المرأة من ذوات الحيض، وإن كانت من ذوات الأشهر يقع في الحال طلقة، وبعد شهر أخرى، وبعد شهر آخر أخرى، وكذا الحامل إن لم يكن له نية أو نوى كذلك، وإن كان قبل الدخول بها وقعت للحال طلقة ثم لا يقع عليها قبل التزوج شيء؛ لأن تقدير هذا الكلام أنت طالق ثلاثاً لوقت السنة، فينصرف إلى السنة في حق كل واحدة منهن وعند الشافعي وأحمد في رواية في مسألة المتن: يقعن في الحال، وعند مالك واحدة والبائن ليس بسني في ظاهر الرواية؛ إذ لا حاجة إلى إثبات زيادة البينونة في الخلاص، والخلع سني سواء كان في حيض أو طهر؛ لأنه لا يمكن تحصيل البدل إلا به. (عيني، فتح)

ثلاثاً للسنة وقع عند
طلقة، كل طهر وإن نوى أن يقع الثلاث الساعة، أو عند كل رف لأي في الحال أي أو نوى
شهر واحدة صحت، ويقعُ طلاق كلّ زوج عاقل بالغ ولو مكرها .
طلقة
فلا يقع طلاق المجنون
أخرى وبعد
مطلقاً
ثلاثاً للسنة ولم ينو شيئاً واللام في قوله: "للسنة" للوقت، ووقت السنة طهر لا جماع فيه. (مص) صحت [ أي نيته ولو كانت آئسة أو صغيرة مدخولا بها فقال ذلك وقعت الساعة واحدة وبعد شهر شهر آخر أخرى. (ع)] أي نيته أي لو قال: أنت طالق ثلاثا للسنة، ونوى وقوع الثلاث جملة أو متفرقاً على الأطهار صح، وقال زفر: لا تصح نيته إذا نوى الثلاث في الحال؛ لأنه نوى ضد السنة، والشيء لا يحتمل ضده، ولنا: أنه نوى ما يحتمله لفظه فصحت نيته؛ لأنه سني وقوعاً من حيث أن وقوع الثلاث جملة عرف بالسنة لا إيقاعاً، فلم يتناوله مطلق كلامه بدون ذكر الثلاث، والاكتفاء بأنت طالق للسنة فقط؛ إذ المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل وهو السني وقوعا وإيقاعاً، وينتظمه عند نيته إذا كان فيه قصور، فلما ذكر الثلاث قولاً فهو من حيث الوقوع سني لا من حيث الإيقاع بقي فيه قصور يحتاج إليه بالنية والحاصل أنهم اختلفوا فيما إذا نوى وقوع الثلاث جملة هل يصح ذكر الثلاث أو لا؟ والراجح أنه لا يصح فيه وقوعها جملة إذا لم يذكر الثلاث. (عيني، فتح) عاقل بالغ: [فلا يقع طلاق الصبي ولو كان البلوغ بالسن والشرط أن يكون الزوج مستيقظاً. (ط،ع)] لقوله عليه "كل طلاق جائز إلا طلاق الصبي والمجنون وحكم المعتوه والمغمى عليه كالمجنون، وكذا لا يقع طلاق النائم، والمعتوه كان قليل الفهم مختلط الكلام فاسد التدبير إلا أنه لا يضرب ولا يشتم. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٤/١] ولو مكرهاً متصلة، أي وإن كان الزوج مكرها على إنشاء ،الطلاق، أما لو أكره على الإقرار بالطلاق فأقر لا ينفذ إقراره. (ط)] أي بالنطق فلو أكره بالحبس والضرب على أن يكتب طلاق امرأته فكتب لا تطلق امرأته؛ لأن الكتابة أقيمت مقام العبارة باعتبار الحاجة ولا حاجة هنا، وقال الشافعي طلاق المكره لا يقع؛ لقوله عليا "رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما استكرهوا عليه وبه قال مالك وأحمد ، ولنا: عموم ما روينا من أن كل طلاق جائز وأيضاً قوله علي ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق والرجعة"، رواه الطحاوي وغيره، وقال الترمذي: حديث حسن، وخرجه الحاكم في "المستدرك".
من
وقال : صحيح الإسناد، والمراد بما رواه أحكام الآخرة؛ لأن عينه ليس بمراد لوجوده حقيقة، وحكمه دنيوي وأخروي، فلا يتناولهما لفظ واحد؛ لأنهما كالمشترك، وحكم الآخرة مراد بالإجماع فانتفى الآخر أن يكون مراداً ثم جملة ما يصح من الأحكام مع الإكراه عشرون الطلاق والنكاح والرجعة والحلف بطلاق أو إعتاق والظهار والإيلاء والعتق وإيجاب الصدقة والعفو عن دم العمد وقبول المرأة الطلاق على مال والإسلام وقبول الصلح عن العمد على مال والتدبير والاستيلاد والرضاع واليمين والنذر والفيء والإكراه على قبول الوديعة. (فتح، عيني)
دم
['To his wife with whom he has intercourse': meaning actually or legally, because seclusion is like intercourse with regard to observing the Sunnah. And his statement: 'A divorce occurs at every purity' because it is unrestricted, so it includes the complete [form]. This is if he did not intend anything, and the woman is one of menstruating women. If she is of those who have monthly cycles, one divorce occurs immediately, then after a month another, and after another month another. Similarly for a pregnant woman if he had no intention or intended likewise. If it was before intercourse with her, one divorce occurs immediately, then nothing occurs before marriage because the estimation of this statement is: 'You are divorced three times for the time of the Sunnah,' so it turns to the Sunnah in regard to each of them. According to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in a narration on the issue of the text: they occur immediately. According to Malik: one divorce, and the irrevocable is not sunni in the apparent narration, because there is no need to establish additional irrevocability in the khulasah. Khul' is sunni whether in menstruation or purity, because the compensation cannot be obtained except by it. (Ayni, Fath)

'Three for the sunnah' so one divorce occurs at each purity. And if he intended that the three occur immediately, or at each raising [of voice?], i.e., immediately, or intended one per month, it is valid. And the divorce of every sane adult husband occurs, even if coerced. So the divorce of a madman does not occur at all. 'Three for the sunnah' and he did not intend anything, and the lam in 'lil-sunnah' is for time, and the time of sunnah is a purity without intercourse. (Mishkat) 'It is valid' [i.e., his intention, even if she is post-menopausal or a minor who was consummated with, and he said that, one divorce occurs immediately, then after a month another, and after another month another. (Ayni)] i.e., his intention: if he said: 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' and intended the three to occur together or separately in the purities, it is valid. Zufar said: his intention is not valid if he intended the three immediately, because he intended the opposite of the sunnah, and a thing cannot bear its opposite. Our proof: he intended what his wording can bear, so his intention is valid, because it is sunni in terms of occurrence in that the occurrence of three together is known by the sunnah not by execution, so it is not covered by his unrestricted speech without mentioning the three. And suffice with 'You are divorced for the sunnah' only, because the unrestricted turns to the complete, which is sunni in occurrence and execution. It is regularized by his intention if there is deficiency. So when he mentioned the three verbally, it is sunni in terms of occurrence not execution, so there remains deficiency that needs intention. The conclusion is that they differed on whether if he intends the three to occur together, is mentioning the three valid? The preponderant view is that it is not valid for them to occur together if he did not mention the three. (Ayni, Fath) 'Sane adult': [So the divorce of a minor does not occur, even if puberty is by age, and the condition is that the husband is awake. (Tahawi, Ayni)] because of his statement 'Every divorce is valid except the divorce of a minor and a madman.' And the ruling of an imbecile and one who is unconscious is like a madman. Similarly, the divorce of a sleeping person does not occur. The imbecile is one of little understanding, confused speech, poor management, but he is not beaten nor insulted. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 234/1] 'Even if coerced' i.e., even if the husband is coerced into initiating the divorce. However, if he is coerced into confessing to divorce and he confesses, his confession does not take effect. (Tahawi)] i.e., by speech. So if he is coerced by imprisonment and beating to write a divorce of his wife and he writes, his wife is not divorced, because writing is treated as speech based on need, and there is no need here. Al-Shafi'i said: the divorce of a coerced person does not occur because of his statement: 'My nation is pardoned for mistakes, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced into.' And Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our proof: the generality of what we narrated that 'Every divorce is valid,' and also his statement: 'Three things, serious and in jest, are serious: marriage, divorce, and taking back.' Narrated by Tahawi and others; Tirmidhi said it is a hasan hadith, and Hakim recorded it in al-Mustadrak. He said: authentic chain. The meaning of what he narrated is the rulings of the Hereafter, because the literal meaning is not intended due to its actual existence, and its ruling is worldly and otherworldly, so one word cannot cover both because they are like homonyms. The otherworldly ruling is intended by consensus, so the other is excluded. Then the total of rulings that are valid with coercion is twenty: divorce, marriage, taking back, swearing by divorce or freeing, zihar, lian, freeing, rendering charity obligatory, pardon for deliberate blood, acceptance of divorce by a woman for compensation, Islam, acceptance of reconciliation for deliberate blood with compensation, tadbir, istilad, breastfeeding, oath, vow, fi', and coercion to accept a deposit. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) rulings on a man saying 'You are divorced three times for the Sunnah' and the effect of intention; (2) the fundamental conditions for talaq to be valid (sane, adult, awake) and the effect of coercion. The first part discusses how the expression 'three for the sunnah' is interpreted: if the woman menstruates, one divorce occurs at each purity; if she is on months (post-menopausal or young), one per month; if pregnant, similarly. The intention of the husband matters: if he intends the three to occur immediately, it is valid because his words can bear that. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi position is that the intention is valid. The correct view is that if he does not mention the number three, the three cannot occur together. The second part states the general principle: the divorce of every sane adult husband is valid, even if he is coerced. Exceptions: minor, insane, sleeping, unconscious. The hadith 'Every divorce is valid except that of a minor and a madman' is cited. The dispute with Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad is addressed: they hold coerced divorce does not occur based on the hadith of pardon for mistakes and coercion. The Hanafi response distinguishes between worldly and otherworldly rulings: the hadith refers to sin in the Hereafter, not worldly legal effect. The text lists twenty rulings that are effective despite coercion. The overall picture is that the Hanafi school is strict on the validity of a husband's divorce, even under coercion, to protect the rights of the wife and prevent manipulation.

Key Terms
سني (sunni): Divorce that conforms to the Sunnah, given in a purity without intercourse.
بدعي (bid'i): Innovative divorce, e.g., during menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' and intends all three to occur immediately, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Only one divorce occurs; the intention is invalid.
B) All three occur immediately.
C) The divorces are spread over three purities regardless of intention.
D) The divorces are suspended until a court ruling.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the husband's intention can override the default timing of a 'three for the sunnah' divorce, provided the number three is explicitly mentioned.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner

Conditions for Valid Talaq: Sanity, Adulthood, and Consciousness
Conditions for valid talaq and exclusionary categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three primary conditions for a valid talaq (adult, sane, awake) and identify which persons are excluded from effecting a divorce.

Core Idea
Only a sane, adult, and conscious husband can issue a valid divorce; all others are legally incapable.

The Hanafi school establishes minimal mental and physical capacity requirements for a husband's pronouncement of talaq to take effect. The text explicitly excludes the minor, the insane, the sleeping, and the unconscious. It also introduces the critical principle that a coerced husband's divorce is valid—a position that sets the stage for the inter-madhhab dispute covered in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positive conditions
The text states: 'the divorce of every sane adult husband occurs'. The conditions are: sanity (aql), adulthood (bulugh), and being awake (yaqzah).
These are shurut al-wujub and shurut al-sihhah.
2
List the excluded persons
The exceptions given: minor (sabi), insane (majnun), sleeping (na'im), unconscious (mughmi 'alayh), and imbecile (ma'tuh). Each lacks either sanity, adulthood, or consciousness.
The imbecile is defined as one of little understanding and confused speech.
3
Note the ruling on coercion
The text says 'even if coerced' (wa law mukrahan), meaning coercion does not invalidate talaq. This is a general principle that will be explored in the dispute lesson.
This is a preliminary statement; the detailed proofs are in the next lesson.

Source Text

(فتح، عيني)
دم
['To his wife with whom he has intercourse': meaning actually or legally, because seclusion is like intercourse with regard to observing the Sunnah. And his statement: 'A divorce occurs at every purity' because it is unrestricted, so it includes the complete [form]. This is if he did not intend anything, and the woman is one of menstruating women. If she is of those who have monthly cycles, one divorce occurs immediately, then after a month another, and after another month another. Similarly for a pregnant woman if he had no intention or intended likewise. If it was before intercourse with her, one divorce occurs immediately, then nothing occurs before marriage because the estimation of this statement is: 'You are divorced three times for the time of the Sunnah,' so it turns to the Sunnah in regard to each of them. According to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in a narration on the issue of the text: they occur immediately. According to Malik: one divorce, and the irrevocable is not sunni in the apparent narration, because there is no need to establish additional irrevocability in the khulasah. Khul' is sunni whether in menstruation or purity, because the compensation cannot be obtained except by it. (Ayni, Fath)

'Three for the sunnah' so one divorce occurs at each purity. And if he intended that the three occur immediately, or at each raising [of voice?], i.e., immediately, or intended one per month, it is valid. And the divorce of every sane adult husband occurs, even if coerced. So the divorce of a madman does not occur at all. 'Three for the sunnah' and he did not intend anything, and the lam in 'lil-sunnah' is for time, and the time of sunnah is a purity without intercourse. (Mishkat) 'It is valid' [i.e., his intention, even if she is post-menopausal or a minor who was consummated with, and he said that, one divorce occurs immediately, then after a month another, and after another month another. (Ayni)] i.e., his intention: if he said: 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' and intended the three to occur together or separately in the purities, it is valid. Zufar said: his intention is not valid if he intended the three immediately, because he intended the opposite of the sunnah, and a thing cannot bear its opposite. Our proof: he intended what his wording can bear, so his intention is valid, because it is sunni in terms of occurrence in that the occurrence of three together is known by the sunnah not by execution, so it is not covered by his unrestricted speech without mentioning the three. And suffice with 'You are divorced for the sunnah' only, because the unrestricted turns to the complete, which is sunni in occurrence and execution. It is regularized by his intention if there is deficiency. So when he mentioned the three verbally, it is sunni in terms of occurrence not execution, so there remains deficiency that needs intention. The conclusion is that they differed on whether if he intends the three to occur together, is mentioning the three valid? The preponderant view is that it is not valid for them to occur together if he did not mention the three. (Ayni, Fath) 'Sane adult': [So the divorce of a minor does not occur, even if puberty is by age, and the condition is that the husband is awake. (Tahawi, Ayni)] because of his statement 'Every divorce is valid except the divorce of a minor and a madman.' And the ruling of an imbecile and one who is unconscious is like a madman. Similarly, the divorce of a sleeping person does not occur. The imbecile is one of little understanding, confused speech, poor management, but he is not beaten nor insulted. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 234/1] 'Even if coerced' i.e., even if the husband is coerced into initiating the divorce. However, if he is coerced into confessing to divorce and he confesses, his confession does not take effect. (Tahawi)] i.e., by speech. So if he is coerced by imprisonment and beating to write a divorce of his wife and he writes, his wife is not divorced, because writing is treated as speech based on need, and there is no need here. Al-Shafi'i said: the divorce of a coerced person does not occur because of his statement: 'My nation is pardoned for mistakes, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced into.' And Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our proof: the generality of what we narrated that 'Every divorce is valid,' and also his statement: 'Three things, serious and in jest, are serious: marriage, divorce, and taking back.' Narrated by Tahawi and others; Tirmidhi said it is a hasan hadith, and Hakim recorded it in al-Mustadrak. He said: authentic chain. The meaning of what he narrated is the rulings of the Hereafter, because the literal meaning is not intended due to its actual existence, and its ruling is worldly and otherworldly, so one word cannot cover both because they are like homonyms. The otherworldly ruling is intended by consensus, so the other is excluded. Then the total of rulings that are valid with coercion is twenty: divorce, marriage, taking back, swearing by divorce or freeing, zihar, lian, freeing, rendering charity obligatory, pardon for deliberate blood, acceptance of divorce by a woman for compensation, Islam, acceptance of reconciliation for deliberate blood with compensation, tadbir, istilad, breastfeeding, oath, vow, fi', and coercion to accept a deposit. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) rulings on a man saying 'You are divorced three times for the Sunnah' and the effect of intention; (2) the fundamental conditions for talaq to be valid (sane, adult, awake) and the effect of coercion. The first part discusses how the expression 'three for the sunnah' is interpreted: if the woman menstruates, one divorce occurs at each purity; if she is on months (post-menopausal or young), one per month; if pregnant, similarly. The intention of the husband matters: if he intends the three to occur immediately, it is valid because his words can bear that. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi position is that the intention is valid. The correct view is that if he does not mention the number three, the three cannot occur together. The second part states the general principle: the divorce of every sane adult husband is valid, even if he is coerced. Exceptions: minor, insane, sleeping, unconscious. The hadith 'Every divorce is valid except that of a minor and a madman' is cited. The dispute with Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad is addressed: they hold coerced divorce does not occur based on the hadith of pardon for mistakes and coercion. The Hanafi response distinguishes between worldly and otherworldly rulings: the hadith refers to sin in the Hereafter, not worldly legal effect. The text lists twenty rulings that are effective despite coercion. The overall picture is that the Hanafi school is strict on the validity of a husband's divorce, even under coercion, to protect the rights of the wife and prevent manipulation.

Key Terms
مكرهاً (mukrahan): Coerced; being forced by threat or duress to perform an action (here, divorce).
معتوه (ma'tuh): An imbecile: a person of little understanding, confused speech, poor management.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following persons can validly pronounce talaq according to the Hanafi school?
A) A 12-year-old boy who has reached puberty by age (14 lunar years?)
B) A man who is awake and sane but coerced under threat of death
C) A sleeping man who mutters 'You are divorced'
D) A man who is unconscious due to a stroke

Key Takeaway
For talaq to be valid, the husband must be adult, sane, and awake; coercion does not invalidate it.

Talaq — Divorce

Coerced Divorce: The Hanafi Position and Its Proofs
Inter-madhhab dispute on coerced divorce with proofs and list of affected rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that coerced divorce is valid, citing the key hadith evidence and responding to the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali objections.

Core Idea
Coerced divorce is valid in Hanafi law because the words are still based on free will in utterance, and worldly effects separate from sin.

This lesson dives into the core inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of coerced talaq. The passage provides the Hanafi proof from well-known hadith ('Three things are serious even in jest' and 'Every divorce is valid except the minor and madman') and then addresses the opposing school's reliance on the hadith of pardon for coercion. The Hanafi response distinguishes between worldly legal effects and otherworldly accountability. The text also lists twenty categories of rulings that remain effective despite coercion.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its primary proof
The Hanafi position is that a coerced divorce is valid. The proof is the hadith: 'Three things, serious and in jest, are serious: marriage, divorce, and taking back.' And also 'Every divorce is valid except that of a minor and a madman.'
These hadith establish the general principle that divorce is not easily invalidated.
2
Identify the opposing proof
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools cite the hadith: 'My nation is pardoned for mistakes, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced into.' They interpret this as covering the legal effects of coerced acts.
This is a strong proof from the Quranic principle of 'no compulsion in religion' extended to talaq.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between worldly rulings (ahkam dunyawi) and otherworldly rulings (ahkam ukhrawi). The hadith of pardon refers to the latter—the person is not sinful—but the worldly legal effect of divorce still applies because the words were uttered.
This is a subtle usul point about the scope of the hadith.
4
List the twenty rulings that are effective despite coercion
The text enumerates twenty types of legal acts that remain valid when done under coercion, including marriage, divorce, freeing slaves, oaths, etc. This shows the general Hanafi principle that coercion does not nullify legal effects of speech.
This list underscores the consistency of the Hanafi approach.

لموطوءته: أي حقيقة أو حكماً؛ لأن الخلوة كالدخول في حق مراعاة السنة، وقوله: "وقع عند كل طهر طلقة"؛ لأنه مطلق فيتناول الكامل هذا إذا لم ينو شيئاً، وكانت المرأة من ذوات الحيض، وإن كانت من ذوات الأشهر يقع في الحال طلقة، وبعد شهر أخرى، وبعد شهر آخر أخرى، وكذا الحامل إن لم يكن له نية أو نوى كذلك، وإن كان قبل الدخول بها وقعت للحال طلقة ثم لا يقع عليها قبل التزوج شيء؛ لأن تقدير هذا الكلام أنت طالق ثلاثاً لوقت السنة، فينصرف إلى السنة في حق كل واحدة منهن وعند الشافعي وأحمد في رواية في مسألة المتن: يقعن في الحال، وعند مالك واحدة والبائن ليس بسني في ظاهر الرواية؛ إذ لا حاجة إلى إثبات زيادة البينونة في الخلاص، والخلع سني سواء كان في حيض أو طهر؛ لأنه لا يمكن تحصيل البدل إلا به. (عيني، فتح)

مطلقاً
ثلاثاً للسنة ولم ينو شيئاً واللام في قوله: "للسنة" للوقت، ووقت السنة طهر لا جماع فيه. (مص) صحت [ أي نيته ولو كانت آئسة أو صغيرة مدخولا بها فقال ذلك وقعت الساعة واحدة وبعد شهر شهر آخر أخرى. (ع)] أي نيته أي لو قال: أنت طالق ثلاثا للسنة، ونوى وقوع الثلاث جملة أو متفرقاً على الأطهار صح، وقال زفر: لا تصح نيته إذا نوى الثلاث في الحال؛ لأنه نوى ضد السنة، والشيء لا يحتمل ضده، ولنا: أنه نوى ما يحتمله لفظه فصحت نيته؛ لأنه سني وقوعاً من حيث أن وقوع الثلاث جملة عرف بالسنة لا إيقاعاً، فلم يتناوله مطلق كلامه بدون ذكر الثلاث، والاكتفاء بأنت طالق للسنة فقط؛ إذ المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل وهو السني وقوعا وإيقاعاً، وينتظمه عند نيته إذا كان فيه قصور، فلما ذكر الثلاث قولاً فهو من حيث الوقوع سني لا من حيث الإيقاع بقي فيه قصور يحتاج إليه بالنية والحاصل أنهم اختلفوا فيما إذا نوى وقوع الثلاث جملة هل يصح ذكر الثلاث أو لا؟ والراجح أنه لا يصح فيه وقوعها جملة إذا لم يذكر الثلاث. (عيني، فتح) عاقل بالغ: [فلا يقع طلاق الصبي ولو كان البلوغ بالسن والشرط أن يكون الزوج مستيقظاً. (ط،ع)] لقوله عليه "كل طلاق جائز إلا طلاق الصبي والمجنون وحكم المعتوه والمغمى عليه كالمجنون، وكذا لا يقع طلاق النائم، والمعتوه كان قليل الفهم مختلط الكلام فاسد التدبير إلا أنه لا يضرب ولا يشتم. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٤/١] ولو مكرهاً متصلة، أي وإن كان الزوج مكرها على إنشاء ،الطلاق، أما لو أكره على الإقرار بالطلاق فأقر لا ينفذ إقراره. (ط)] أي بالنطق فلو أكره بالحبس والضرب على أن يكتب طلاق امرأته فكتب لا تطلق امرأته؛ لأن الكتابة أقيمت مقام العبارة باعتبار الحاجة ولا حاجة هنا، وقال الشافعي طلاق المكره لا يقع؛ لقوله عليا "رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما استكرهوا عليه وبه قال مالك وأحمد ، ولنا: عموم ما روينا من أن كل طلاق جائز وأيضاً قوله علي ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق والرجعة"، رواه الطحاوي وغيره، وقال الترمذي: حديث حسن، وخرجه الحاكم في "المستدرك".
من
وقال : صحيح الإسناد، والمراد بما رواه أحكام الآخرة؛ لأن عينه ليس بمراد لوجوده حقيقة، وحكمه دنيوي وأخروي، فلا يتناولهما لفظ واحد؛ لأنهما كالمشترك، وحكم الآخرة مراد بالإجماع فانتفى الآخر أن يكون مراداً ثم جملة ما يصح من الأحكام مع الإكراه عشرون الطلاق والنكاح والرجعة والحلف بطلاق أو إعتاق والظهار والإيلاء والعتق وإيجاب الصدقة والعفو عن دم العمد وقبول المرأة الطلاق على مال والإسلام وقبول الصلح عن العمد على مال والتدبير والاستيلاد والرضاع واليمين والنذر والفيء والإكراه على قبول الوديعة. ['To his wife with whom he has intercourse': meaning actually or legally, because seclusion is like intercourse with regard to observing the Sunnah. And his statement: 'A divorce occurs at every purity' because it is unrestricted, so it includes the complete [form]. This is if he did not intend anything, and the woman is one of menstruating women. If she is of those who have monthly cycles, one divorce occurs immediately, then after a month another, and after another month another. Similarly for a pregnant woman if he had no intention or intended likewise. If it was before intercourse with her, one divorce occurs immediately, then nothing occurs before marriage because the estimation of this statement is: 'You are divorced three times for the time of the Sunnah,' so it turns to the Sunnah in regard to each of them. It is regularized by his intention if there is deficiency. So when he mentioned the three verbally, it is sunni in terms of occurrence not execution, so there remains deficiency that needs intention. However, if he is coerced into confessing to divorce and he confesses, his confession does not take effect. (Tahawi)] i.e., by speech. So if he is coerced by imprisonment and beating to write a divorce of his wife and he writes, his wife is not divorced, because writing is treated as speech based on need, and there is no need here. Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) rulings on a man saying 'You are divorced three times for the Sunnah' and the effect of intention; (2) the fundamental conditions for talaq to be valid (sane, adult, awake) and the effect of coercion. The first part discusses how the expression 'three for the sunnah' is interpreted: if the woman menstruates, one divorce occurs at each purity; if she is on months (post-menopausal or young), one per month; if pregnant, similarly. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi position is that the intention is valid. The correct view is that if he does not mention the number three, the three cannot occur together. The second part states the general principle: the divorce of every sane adult husband is valid, even if he is coerced. Exceptions: minor, insane, sleeping, unconscious. The hadith 'Every divorce is valid except that of a minor and a madman' is cited. The dispute with Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad is addressed: they hold coerced divorce does not occur based on the hadith of pardon for mistakes and coercion. The Hanafi response distinguishes between worldly and otherworldly rulings: the hadith refers to sin in the Hereafter, not worldly legal effect. The text lists twenty rulings that are effective despite coercion. The overall picture is that the Hanafi school is strict on the validity of a husband's divorce, even under coercion, to protect the rights of the wife and prevent manipulation.

Key Terms
مكرهاً (mukrahan): Coerced; being forced by threat or duress to perform an action (here, divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the opposing school's hadith that 'My nation is pardoned for what they are coerced into'?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
B) The hadith refers only to the Hereafter (sin), not worldly legal effects.
C) The hadith is abrogated by the hadith about three things being serious.
D) The hadith applies only to acts of worship, not to divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a coerced divorce is valid because the worldly legal effect of the spoken words is not nullified by duress; the husband's sin is forgiven, but the talaq stands.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Intention for Immediate Triple Divorce: Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar
Dispute over valid intention when saying 'three for the sunna'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of intending immediate triple divorce when saying 'three for the sunna', and explain Zufar's objection and the response.

Core Idea
The wording 'for the sunna' can bear the meaning of occurrence, so intention for immediate triple is valid only if the word 'three' is spoken.

This passage deals with a subtle point in talaq: when a husband says 'You are divorced three for the sunna', does his intention for immediate triple divorce take effect? Abu Hanifa and Zufar, both within the Hanafi school, differ. Understanding this dispute requires distinguishing between sunna in performance versus sunna in occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The husband says 'three for the sunna'. The term 'for the sunna' can refer to the time (pure period) or the method (one per period).
2
Identify the two intentions
The husband may intend the three to occur immediately (all at once) or separately over three pure periods.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
If he mentions 'three' and intends immediate occurrence, it is valid because the wording can bear that meaning; the occurrence is sunni (known from sunna) even if the performance is not.
4
State Zufar's objection
Immediate triple is the opposite of sunna, so the wording cannot bear that intention.
5
Explain the response and mufta bihi
The occurrence of triple talaq together is itself known from sunna, so the wording can bear it. The preponderant view is that if he does not mention 'three', his intention for immediate triple is invalid; only one talaq occurs.
Tarjih from Ayni and Fath al-Qadir

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
ثلاثاً للسنة وقع عند
أقسام الطلاق وأحكامها
طلقة، كل طهر وإن نوى أن يقع الثلاث الساعة، أو عند كل رف لأي في الحال أي أو نوى شهر واحدة صحت، ويقعُ طلاق كلّ زوج عاقل بالغ ولو مكرها .

أخرى وبعد
ثلاثاً للسنة ولم ينو شيئاً واللام في قوله: "للسنة" للوقت، ووقت السنة طهر لا جماع فيه. (مص) صحت [ أي نيته ولو كانت آئسة أو صغيرة مدخولا بها فقال ذلك وقعت الساعة واحدة وبعد شهر شهر آخر أخرى. (ع)] أي نيته أي لو قال: أنت طالق ثلاثا للسنة، ونوى وقوع الثلاث جملة أو متفرقاً على الأطهار صح، وقال زفر: لا تصح نيته إذا نوى الثلاث في الحال؛ لأنه نوى ضد السنة، والشيء لا يحتمل ضده، ولنا: أنه نوى ما يحتمله لفظه فصحت نيته؛ لأنه سني وقوعاً من حيث أن وقوع الثلاث جملة عرف بالسنة لا إيقاعاً، فلم يتناوله مطلق كلامه بدون ذكر الثلاث، والاكتفاء بأنت طالق للسنة فقط؛ إذ المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل وهو السني وقوعا وإيقاعاً، وينتظمه عند نيته إذا كان فيه قصور، فلما ذكر الثلاث قولاً فهو من حيث الوقوع سني لا من حيث الإيقاع بقي فيه قصور يحتاج إليه بالنية والحاصل أنهم اختلفوا فيما إذا نوى وقوع الثلاث جملة هل يصح ذكر الثلاث أو لا؟ والراجح أنه لا يصح فيه وقوعها جملة إذا لم يذكر الثلاث. (عيني، فتح)
Book of Divorce. Chapter: Divisions of Divorce and Their Rulings. [If he says] 'three for the sunna' [and he intended] each period of purity, and if he intended that the three occur immediately, or at each [period?], or if he intended one month, it is valid. And the divorce of every sane, adult husband is valid, even if coerced. Another talaq and after three for the sunna and he did not intend anything, and the lam in his statement 'for the sunna' is for time, and the time of sunna is a purity in which there is no intercourse. (Misbah) It is valid [i.e., his intention, even if the wife is post-menopausal or a minor who has been consummated with, if he said that, it occurs immediately one, and after a month another, and after another another. (Ayni)] i.e., his intention, i.e., if he said: 'You are divorced three for the sunna', and he intended the occurrence of the three together or separately over the purities, it is valid. Zufar said: His intention is not valid if he intended the three immediately because he intended the opposite of sunna, and a thing cannot bear its opposite. Our proof: He intended what his wording can bear, so his intention is valid, because it is sunni in occurrence in that the occurrence of three together is known by the sunna, not in performance. So his absolute speech without mentioning three does not include it, and being satisfied with 'you are divorced for the sunna' alone; because the absolute refers to the perfect, which is sunni in occurrence and performance, and it is regulated by his intention if there is deficiency, so when he mentioned three verbally, it is sunni in occurrence not in performance, a deficiency remains that needs intention. The gist is that they differed whether it is valid to intend a single occurrence of three together if he mentioned three or not? The preponderant view is that it is not valid for them to occur together if he did not mention three. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is the validity of a husband's intention when he says 'You are divorced three for the sunna' ('anti taliq thalathan li al-sunnah'). The sunna divorce is to give one talaq per purity period without intercourse. However, the wording 'for the sunna' can also refer to the time of sunna (a pure period). The author explains that if the husband intended the three divorces to occur immediately (all at once), his intention is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but Zufar disagrees because he considers immediate triple divorce contrary to sunna. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the wording 'for the sunna' can bear the meaning of occurrence (sunni in effect) even if the performance is not sunna. The preponderant view (rajih) is that if he did not explicitly mention the word 'three', then the intention of immediate triple divorce is not valid; only one talaq occurs. Therefore, mentioning 'three' is crucial for the validity of intending all three at once.

Key Terms
لسنة (li al-sunnah): Refers to time of sunna (a pure period without intercourse) or to the sunna method of divorce.
ثلاثاً (thalathan): The number three, indicating three talaqs in one utterance.
سني وقوعاً (sunnī wuqū‘an): Sunni in occurrence: the fact of three divorces happening together is established in the sunna (e.g., by prophetic silence or practice).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant view in this passage, what is required for the intention of immediate triple talaq to be valid when saying 'three for the sunna'?
A) The husband must intend all three to occur at once
B) The husband must explicitly mention the word 'three' in his utterance
C) The wife must be in a pure period with no intercourse
D) The intention is always valid regardless of wording

Key Takeaway
When a husband says 'three for the sunna', his intention for immediate triple divorce is valid only if he includes the word 'three'; otherwise, only one talaq occurs.
