Conditional Divorce on Emancipation of the Wife's Master
Ruling on talaq conditioned on emancipation of the wife's master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband conditions divorce on the emancipation of his wife's master and explain why the husband retains the right of return.

Core Idea
Condition precedes conditioned: emancipation occurs first, so divorce falls while wife is free.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi family law: a conditional divorce linked to a third party's action. Understanding the temporal order of condition and conditioned is crucial for correct application. We will see how the husband's retention of the right of return depends on the wife's status at the moment divorce takes effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the condition
The husband says to his wife (who is a slave belonging to another): 'You are divorced two with the emancipation of your master.' The condition is the master's act of freeing her.
The statement is a conditional divorce, not an immediate one.
2
Order the events: condition precedes conditioned
According to Hanafi usul, the condition must occur before the conditioned event. Thus, the master's emancipation happens first.
This is based on the principle that the condition (shart) is prior to the conditioned (mashrut).
3
Determine the wife's legal status at the moment of divorce
Since emancipation occurs first, at the moment the divorce takes effect, the wife is free. She was a slave when the statement was made but free when the divorce actually occurs.
This is critical because the number and revocability of divorces depend on her status.
4
Apply the Hanafi ruling
A free woman divorced by two pronouncements is not permanently prohibited. The divorce is revocable (talaq raj'i). Thus, two revocable divorces occur, and the husband has the right to take her back during the 'iddah.
If she were still a slave at divorce, the ruling would differ (e.g., one revocable divorce? Actually, per Hanafi, slave woman is also divorced by two revocably? But the passage emphasizes the free status).
5
Recognize the underlying usul principle
The reasoning illustrates the rule: 'al-shart qabl al-mashrut' (the condition comes before the conditioned). This is a foundational principle in legal cause and effect.
This principle is not unique to divorce but applies broadly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنت طالق: أي لو قال لامرأته وهي أمة غيره: أنت طالق إلخ. (ط) فأعتق: أي المولى الأمة طلقت ثنتين. (ع) له الرجعة: [ أي للزوج الرجعة؛ لأنه طلق وهي حرة والحرة لا تحرم بالطلقتين حرمة غليظة. (ع)] أي إذا قال لامرأته وهي أمة لغيره: أنت طالق ثنتين مع عتق ،مولاك، فأعتقها مولاها ملك الزوج الرجعة؛ لأن معنى قوله: 'مع عتق مولاك' مع إعتاق مولاك؛ إذ العتق قد يستعمل متعديا، ثم لما كان إعتاق المولى شرطا للتطليق فلا بد أن يكون مقدماً عليه؛ لأن الشرط يكون مقدما على المشروط، فالعتق يكون مقدماً على وقوع الطلاق، فيقع الطلاق حال كونها حرة، - أيضاً يقع؛
'You are divorced': i.e., if he says to his wife while she is a slave belonging to another: 'You are divorced' etc. (T) 'so he emancipates': i.e., the master of the female slave emancipates her, she is divorced two. (Ayni) 'He has the right of return (raj'a)': [Ayni: i.e., the husband has the right of return because he divorced her while she was free, and a free woman is not prohibited by two divorces permanently. (Ayni)] That is, if he says to his wife who is a slave belonging to someone else: 'You are divorced two with the emancipation of your master', and her master frees her, the husband retains the right of return; because the meaning of his statement 'with the emancipation of your master' is 'with your master's emancipating; since emancipation is sometimes used transitively. Then, since the emancipation by the master is a condition for the pronouncement of divorce, it must be prior to it; because the condition comes before the conditioned. So the emancipation occurs before the divorce, and thus the divorce occurs while she is free.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on a specific conditional divorce scenario. A husband says to his wife, who is a slave belonging to another master: 'You are divorced two with the emancipation of your master.' The condition is the master's emancipation. When the master emancipates her, the divorce takes effect, because the emancipation occurs first (as a condition precedent), so at the moment of divorce she is free. Since a free woman is not permanently prohibited by two divorces, the husband retains the right to take her back (raj'a) during her 'iddah. The reasoning explains that 'with' here means 'at the time of' and the condition is prior. The text also clarifies that the statement is valid and the divorce occurs.

Key Terms
الرجعة (al-raj'a): The right to take back a wife during the 'iddah of a revocable divorce.
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave.
شرط (shart): Condition; a prerequisite that must be fulfilled for a legal effect to occur.
مشروط (mashrut): The conditioned effect; the legal consequence that depends on the condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife who is a slave owned by another: 'You are divorced two with the emancipation of your master', and the master frees her, what is the ruling?
A) No divorce occurs; the condition is invalid.
B) One revocable divorce occurs.
C) Two irrevocable divorces occur.
D) Two revocable divorces occur, and the husband has the right of return.

Key Takeaway
A valid conditional divorce linked to a future event takes effect only after the condition is fulfilled, and the ruling is based on the wife's status at that moment.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
5 min
Divorce Added to Time of Death is Void
Opening ruling on conditional divorce tied to death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a divorce conditioned upon the death of either spouse is void and explain the legal reasoning based on capacity and suitability.

Core Idea
A divorce tied to death is void because death destroys the husband's capacity or the wife's suitability for divorce.

The passage opens with a clear ruling: adding divorce to a future time such as 'my death' or 'your death' renders the pronouncement void and without effect. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi divorce law, rooted in the necessity of both parties possessing legal capacity and the marital bond being intact at the moment of divorce. We will analyze the consensus on this point and the rationale behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional divorce scenario
The husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced upon my death' or 'upon your death'. Recognize that this attaches divorce to a future event that ends the marriage or the husband's capacity.
2
State the ruling
The text says such pronouncements are 'laghw' (void) by scholarly agreement.
The term 'laghw' means it has no legal effect.
3
Analyze the reason for voidness
For divorce to be valid, the husband must have legal capacity (ahliyyah) to divorce, and the wife must be a suitable subject (mahalliyyah) for divorce. The husband's death negates his capacity; the wife's death negates her suitability. Thus the condition defeats the essential prerequisites.
This is a talil (causal reasoning) based on the nature of divorce.
4
Confirm the consensus
The text states 'by agreement' (bil-ittifaq), indicating unanimity among Hanafi scholars, and likely across schools, on this point.
No ikhtilaf is reported here.

كتاب الطلاق أو 611 إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان مع موتي أو مع موتك لغو، ولو ملكها أو شقصها أو ملكته أو شقصه بطل العقد أي ملكت المرأة الزوج فلو اشتراها وطلقها لم يقع، أنت طالق ثنتين مع عتق مولاك إياك فأعتق له الرجعة، أي اشترى الزوج منكوحته ومعنى المولى الأمة ولو كان الوقوع بالوصف لكان ذكر الثلاث لغواً، فثبت أن الواقع في الحقيقة إنما هو المنعوت المحذوف، "أنت طالق واحدة" أنت طالق تطليقة واحدة، فإذا كان الواقع هو المنعوت بالعدد، وكان الشك داخلاً في الإيقاع، فلا يقع بالشك، والثانية: لو قال لها: أنت طالق مع موتي والثالثة قال لها: أنت طالق مع موتك، فهاتان ليستا بشيء بالاتفاق؛ لأنه أضاف الطلاق إلى حالة منافية للطلاق؛ لأن موته ينافي أهلية الطلاق، وموتها تنافي المحلية، ولابد من كل واحد من الأهلية والمحلية ليثبت جواز التصرف. (مستخلص) إذا ملكت هي زوجها، ولو ملكها: أي لو ملك الزوج امرأته بأن كانت أمة فاشتراها وورثها ونحو ذلك. (ع) أو شقصها: أي ملك جزءاً منها بأن اشترى نصفها أو ورث النصف أو الثلث. (ع) بطل العقد: أما في ملك الزوج إياها؛ فلأن إثبات الملك على الحرة كان للحاجة إلى إبقاء النسل، وكان ملك النكاح للضرورة، وقد اندفعت بقيام ملك اليمين وأما في ملكها إياه فللاجتماع بين المالكية والمملوكية، لا يقال: الحل لا يثبت بملك البعض؛ لأنا نقول: ملك اليمين دليل الحل، فقام مقام الحل تيسيراً، والحاصل: أنه فالاجتماع بين المالكية والمملوكية يمنع ابتداء النكاح فكذا بقاءه، وإذا ملك الزوج امرأته؛ فلأن ملك اليمين أقوى، فلا يزاحمها الأدنى، أي ملك النكاح بل ينفسخ بوجوده، فإن قلت: المكاتب إذا اشترى زوجته لا يبطل النكاح، قلت: ليس له ملك بل له حق الملك، وهو لا يمنع بقاء النكاح. (عيني، مستخلص، فتح) فلو اشتراها وطلقها لم يقع شيء دخل بها أو لم يدخل، وتجب العدة اتفاقاً؛ لأنه قد وقعت الفرقة بينهما بملك الرقبة، والطلاق يستدعي قيام ملك النكاح من وجه و لم يوجد، وإذا ملكت المرأة الزوج كله أو بعضاً منه ثم طلقها أنه فكذلك لا يقع الطلاق عند الشيخين، وعن محمد لأن العدة واجبة هنا اتفاقاً، وقيام العقد من وجه يكفي لوقوع الطلاق عليها، بخلاف ما إذا ملكها هو؛ لأنه لا عدة عليها هناك حتى حل وطؤها، قلنا: العدة واجبة هناك حتى لا يجوز له أن يزوجها من غيره حتى تنقضي عدتها، ولو أعتقها ظهرت العدة، وإنما لم تظهر بالنسبة إليه لحل وطئها له بملك اليمين، فتبين أن هذا الفرق غير صحيح (رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/١] (فتح) أنت طالق: أي لو قال لامرأته وهي أمة غيره: أنت طالق إلخ. (ط) فأعتق: أي المولى الأمة طلقت ثنتين. (ع) له الرجعة: [ أي للزوج الرجعة؛ لأنه طلق وهي حرة والحرة لا تحرم بالطلقتين حرمة غليظة. (ع)] أي إذا قال لامرأته وهي أمة لغيره: أنت طالق ثنتين مع عتق مولاك، فأعتقها مولاها ملك الزوج الرجعة؛ لأن معنى قوله: "مع عتق مولاك" مع إعتاق مولاك؛ إذ العتق قد يستعمل متعديا، ثم لما كان إعتاق المولى شرطا للتطليق فلا بد أن يكون مقدماً عليه؛ لأن الشرط يكون مقدما على المشروط، فالعتق يكون مقدماً على وقوع الطلاق، فيقع الطلاق حال كونها حرة، -أيضاً يقع؛ كتاب الطلاق ٤١٢ إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان أنت ولو تعلّق عتقها وطلقتاها بمجيء الغد فجاء الغد لا، وعدتها ثلاث حيض، في الصورتين بالإجماع للاحتياط طالق هكذا، وأشار بثلاث أصابع فهي ثلاث، أنت طالق بائن أو البتة = الأمة تعلقت طلقتاها أيضاً أي إشارته هذه فيصير طلاقها ثلاثا، فيملك الرجعة، فإن قيل: إن كلمة "مع" للقران فينبغي وقوع الطلاق، والعتق معاً فكيف هذا؟ قلنا: قد جاء كلمة "مع" للتأخير كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرا (الشرح:٦) أي بعد العسر يسراً؛ لأن العسر مع اليسر أمران متضادان لا يجتمعان فكذا هنا يصير للتأخير. (عيني، مستخلص) الغد بأن قال لها مولاها: إذا جاء غد فأنت حرة، أو قال لها زوجها : إذا جاء غد فأنت طالق ثنتين. (ع) فجاء الغد لا أي عتقت الأمة، وطلقت مغلظة و لم تحل للزوج حتى تنكح زوجا غيره، ولا يملك الزوج الرجعة عند الشيخين، وعند محمد له الرجعة؛ لأن العتق والطلاق لما تعلقا بشرط واحد وهو مجيء الغد، والعتق أسرع وقوعا؛ لكونه رجوعا إلى الحالة الأصلية، وهو أمر مستحسن مندوب إليه، شرعا، بخلاف الطلاق؛ فإنه أبغض المباحات، وجب أن تطلق زمن نزول الحرية فيصادفها الطلاق وهي حرة فلا تحرم بالتطليقتين حرمة غليظة كما في المسألة الأولى، ولهما: أنه علق طلاقها بما علق به المولى عتقها ثم العتق يصادفها وهي أمة فكذا الطلاق فتحرم بتطليقتين حرمة غليظة؛ لأن زمان ثبوت العتق هو زمان ثبوت الطلاق ضرورة تعلقهما بشرط واحد، بخلاف المسألة الأولى؛ لأن فيها علق التطليق بإعتاق المولى، فيقع بعد العتق. (مستخلص، فتح) وعدتها ثلاث حيض أي بالاتفاق احتياطاً، ولو كان الزوج مريضا لا ترث منه؛ لأنه حين تكلم بالطلاق لم تكن لها أهلية الإرث وقت التكلم، فلم يوجد شرط إرثها منه وهو قصد الفرار، أما إذا وجد تعليق الزوج الطلاق في مرضه بعد علمه بحصول تعليق المولى حريتها على مجيء الغد ترث منه عند محمد. (فتح) فهي ثلاث [ أي ثلاث طلقات ولو أشار بأصابعه ولم يقل هكذا فهي واحدة (ط)] لأن الإشارة بالأصابع تفيد العلم بالعدد عرفاً وشرعاً إذا اقترنت بالاسم المبهم، قال عليه : الشهر هكذا وهكذا وهكذا" أشار بأصابعه العشرة ثلاثين يوماً، ثم قال الشهر هكذا وهكذا وهكذا"، وخنس إبهامه في يعني الثالثة تسعة وعشرين يوماً، والإشارة يعني تقع بالمنشورة منها دون المضمومة؛ لأنه عليها لما خنس إبهامه المرة الثالثة فهم منه تسعة وعشرون يوما، ولو اعتبرت المضمومة لكان المفهوم أحدا وعشرين يوما، فالمعتبر المنشور مطلقا للعرف وللسنة. ولو أشار بالواحدة طلقت واحدة، ولو أشار بالثنتين طلقت ثنتين، ولو أشار بثلاث أصابع وقال: عنيت الإشارة بالمضمومتين صدق ديانة لا قضاء، وكذا لو نوى الإشارة بالكف ولو قال: أنت طالق" وأشار بأصابعه ولم يقل: "هكذا فهي واحدة؛ لأن الإشارة تفسير للمبهم من العدد، ولم يوجد فلغت الإشارة ويبقى، قوله: "أنت طالق" وهو لا يحتمل العدد. [تبيين الحقائق: ٦٨/٣] (عيني، فتح طالق بائن أو البتة انتصابها على المصدرية من بت أمره إذا قطع فيه وجزم. (ع)] شروع في بيان وقوع البائن بوصف الطلاق بما ينبئ عن الشدة والزيادة، والبت مصدر بت أمره إذا قطع به، ولو نوى بطالق واحدة وبنحو بائن أخرى يقع ثنتان بائنتان. (فتح)
Book of Divorce or 611 Addition of Divorce to Time: With my death or with your death is void. And if he owns her or a share of her, or she owns him or a share of him, the marriage contract is void. That is, the woman owned the husband. So if he buys her and divorces her, it does not occur. You are divorced twice upon the emancipation of your master, so if he emancipates, he has the right to take her back. That is, the husband bought his wife. And the meaning of master is the slave-owner. And if the occurrence were by description, the mention of three would be useless. So it is established that the actual occurrence is only the described entity that is omitted. The phrase 'you are divorced one' means one divorce. So if the actual occurrence is the entity described by the number, and doubt enters into the occurrence, it does not occur by doubt. The second: if he said to her: You are divorced upon my death. The third: he said to her: You are divorced upon your death. These two are nothing by agreement, because he added divorce to a state contrary to divorce; because his death negates the capacity for divorce, and her death negates the capability. And each of capacity and capability is necessary for the permissibility of the act. (Mukhtasar) If she owns her husband, and if he owns her: i.e., if the husband owns his wife, as if she was a slave and he bought her, inherited her, etc. (Ayni) Or a share of her: i.e., he owns a part of her, such as buying half or inheriting half or third. (Ayni) The contract becomes void. As for the husband owning her, because establishing ownership over a free woman was for the need of preserving progeny, and the ownership of marriage was for necessity, and it has been removed by the existence of right-hand ownership. And as for her owning him, because of the combination of being an owner and owned. It cannot be said that permissibility is not established by owning part, because we say: right-hand ownership is evidence of permissibility, so it stands in place of permissibility for facilitation. The conclusion: the combination of being an owner and owned prevents the initiation of marriage, and likewise its continuation. And if the husband owns his wife, because right-hand ownership is stronger, so the weaker, i.e., the ownership of marriage, does not compete with it; rather it is dissolved by its existence. If you say: a mukatib who buys his wife does not nullify the marriage, I say: he does not have ownership but rather a right to ownership, and that does not prevent the continuation of marriage. (Ayni, Mukhtasar, Fath) So if he buys her and divorces her, nothing occurs, whether he has consummated or not, and the waiting period is obligatory by agreement, because separation has occurred between them by ownership of the neck, and divorce requires the existence of marriage ownership in some respect, and it did not exist. And if the woman owns the husband entirely or partially, then she divorces him, similarly divorce does not occur according to the two shaykhs. And from Muhammad: because the waiting period is obligatory here by agreement, and the existence of the contract in some respect is sufficient for divorce to occur upon her, unlike if he owns her, because there is no waiting period on her until her intercourse is permissible. We say: the waiting period is obligatory there, so that he may not marry her to another until her waiting period ends. And if he emancipates her, the waiting period appears, but it did not appear with respect to him because of the permissibility of intercourse on his part by right-hand ownership. So it becomes clear that this distinction is not correct. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/240, Fath) 'You are divorced': i.e., if he says to his wife who is a slave of another: You are divorced, etc. (T) So if he emancipates: i.e., the master emancipates the slave, she is divorced twice. (Ayni) He has the right to take her back (Ayni) i.e., the husband has the right to take her back because he divorced her while she was free, and a free woman is not prohibited by two divorces with severe prohibition. (Ayni) That is, if he says to his wife who is a slave of another: 'You are divorced twice upon the emancipation of your master', and her master emancipates her, the husband retains the right to take her back. Because the meaning of his words 'upon the emancipation of your master' is 'with the emancipation of your master', since emancipation may be used transitively. Then, since the master's emancipation is a condition for the divorce, it must be prior to it, because the condition is prior to the conditioned. So the emancipation is prior to the occurrence of divorce, so the divorce occurs while she is free. - also it occurs. Book of Divorce 412 Addition of Divorce to Time: 'You are divorced' and if her emancipation and her two divorces are tied to the coming of tomorrow, then tomorrow comes, no, and her waiting period is three menstrual cycles in both cases, by consensus for precaution. 'You are divorced like this' and he pointed with three fingers, so it is three. 'You are divorced irrevocably or absolutely' = the slave woman, her two divorces are also tied. That is, his pointing; so her divorce becomes three, so he retains the right to take her back. If it is said: the word 'with' indicates conjunction, so divorce and emancipation should occur together, so how is this? We say: the word 'with' has come to indicate delay, as in the verse of the Most High: 'Indeed, with hardship comes ease' (94:6), meaning after hardship comes ease, because hardship and ease are two opposite things that cannot be together. So here too it indicates delay. (Ayni, Mukhtasar) 'Tomorrow' meaning: if her master says to her: 'When tomorrow comes, you are free', or her husband says to her: 'When tomorrow comes, you are divorced twice' (Ayni), then tomorrow comes: no. That is, the slave woman is emancipated and divorced with severe prohibition, and she is not permissible for the husband until she marries another husband, and the husband does not have the right to take her back according to the two shaykhs. According to Muhammad, he has the right to take her back, because when the emancipation and divorce are both tied to one condition, which is the coming of tomorrow, and emancipation occurs faster because it is a return to the original state and is a praised, recommended thing in sharia, unlike divorce which is the most hated of permissible things, it becomes necessary that she be divorced at the time of descending upon freedom, so divorce meets her while she is free, and thus she is not prohibited by two divorces with severe prohibition as in the first case. Their evidence: he tied her divorce to that which the master tied her emancipation, and then emancipation meets her while she is a slave, so likewise divorce, so she is prohibited by two divorces with severe prohibition, because the time of establishing emancipation is the time of establishing divorce necessarily due to their being tied to one condition, unlike the first case, because in that case the divorce was tied to the master's act of emancipation, so it occurs after emancipation. (Mukhtasar, Fath) And her waiting period is three menstrual cycles by agreement for precaution. And if the husband is sick, she does not inherit from him, because at the time he spoke the divorce, she did not have capacity for inheritance at the time of speaking, so the condition of her inheriting from him, which is the intention of flight, did not exist. As for if the husband's tying of divorce occurred during his illness after he knew of the master's tying of her freedom to the coming of tomorrow, she inherits from him according to Muhammad. (Fath) So it is three (i.e., three divorces, and if he pointed with his fingers and did not say 'like this', it is one (T)) because pointing with fingers informs of the number by custom and law when accompanied by an ambiguous noun. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The month is like this, like this, like this' and he pointed with all his ten fingers, thirty days. Then he said: 'The month is like this, like this, like this' and he bent his thumb in the third time, meaning twenty-nine days. And the pointing is interpreted with the outstretched fingers, not the closed ones, because when he bent his thumb the third time, twenty-nine days was understood. If the closed ones were considered, the understanding would be twenty-one days. So the outstretched ones are considered absolutely, due to custom and the sunnah. And if he pointed with one, she is divorced once; if he pointed with two, she is divorced twice; if he pointed with three fingers and said: 'I meant the pointing with the closed ones', he is believed in his intention (diyaanatan) but not in court. Similarly, if he intended pointing with the palm. And if he said: 'You are divorced' and pointed with his fingers and did not say 'like this', it is one, because pointing is an interpretation of the ambiguous number, and it did not occur, so the pointing is invalid, and his words 'You are divorced' remain, and that does not take number. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3/68) (Ayni, Fath) 'Divorced irrevocably or absolutely' its grammatical accusative due to being a verbal noun from 'batta' meaning to cut decisively. (Ayni) This is a beginning of explaining the occurrence of irrevocable divorce by description of divorce that indicates severity and increase. 'Al-batt' is the verbal noun of 'batta amrahu' when he decides it. And if he intended by 'taliq' one and by something like 'bain' another, two irrevocable divorces occur. (Fath)
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) expanding on rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding divorce. It covers several distinct issues: (1) Adding divorce to a future time such as death is void by consensus because death negates either the husband's capacity (ahliyyah) or the wife's suitability (mahalliyyah) for divorce. (2) If either spouse acquires ownership of the other (wholly or partially), the marriage contract is automatically voided. The reasoning is that right-hand ownership (milk al-yamin) is stronger than marriage ownership (milk al-nikah), so the latter cannot coexist with it. An exception is a mukatib (slave for a contract of manumission) who does not actually own his wife but has a right to ownership. (3) If the husband buys his wife (who is a slave) and then divorces her, the divorce does not take effect, but iddah remains obligatory because separation occurred via ownership rather than divorce. (4) If the wife owns the husband, divorce also does not occur according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad argues that it does because the contract subsists in some respect, but the preferred position (mufta bihi) is the former. (5) A separate scenario: if a man says to his wife who is a slave of another: 'You are divorced twice upon your master's emancipation,' and the master emancipates her, then two divorces occur and the husband retains the right to take her back because the emancipation precedes the divorce (the word 'ma'a' is interpreted as meaning delay, like in the Quranic verse). (6) If both emancipation and divorce are tied to a single condition (e.g., coming of tomorrow), then when the condition occurs, the emancipation happens simultaneously with the divorce. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this results in an irrevocable three-fold prohibition because she was still a slave at the moment of divorce; Muhammad holds that emancipation occurs first, so she is free at the time of divorce, hence only two divorces occur and husband retains the right to take back. (7) The iddah in such cases is three menstrual cycles by consensus. (8) If the husband was sick at the time of pronouncing the conditional divorce, she does not inherit from him unless he knew of the emancipation condition and intended to divest her of inheritance. (9) Pointing with fingers during talaq: if the husband says 'you are divorced' and points with three outstretched fingers, it counts as three; if he says 'like this' and points with one finger, it is one; if he points without saying 'haka' (like this), it is only one because the pointing is an interpretation of the ambiguous and is ignored. (10) The terms 'bain' or 'al-batta' indicate an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain); if the husband intends by 'taliq' one and by 'bain' another, two irrevocable divorces occur.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Void; having no legal effect.
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the ability to perform valid legal acts.
محلية (mahalliyyah): Suitability of the subject; the wife must be capable of being divorced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'You are divorced upon my death.' What is the ruling?
A) The divorce takes effect at the moment of death.
B) The divorce is void; the marriage continues.
C) The divorce is suspended and becomes effective after iddah.
D) The husband must repeat the divorce after death for it to be valid.

Key Takeaway
Divorce tied to death is void because the condition undermines the essential prerequisites for divorce: the husband's capacity and the wife's suitability.
